Rulings on Water with Uncertainty of Impurity
Concludes water types with practical rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on using water when impurity is uncertain, and distinguish between water that is pure and purifying.

Core Idea
Water is presumed pure until certainty of impurity; flowing water requires a change in attribute; water from a donkey or mule is pure but not purifying.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya provides practical relief for Muslims dealing with water of uncertain purity. It clarifies the relied-upon position for the minimum quantity of large water, the permissibility of using water from containers and wells in the absence of certainty, and the criteria for flowing water to become impure. It also introduces the concept of water doubtful in purifying ability, using the example of water drunk by a donkey or mule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage begins with 'توسعة على الناس' (relief for people), indicating a principle of ease. State the general rule: water is considered pure (tahir) unless there is certainty (yaqeen) of impurity.
This is based on the hadith: 'إن الماء طهور لا ينجسه شيء' (Water is pure and purifying; nothing makes it impure).
2
Examine the rulings on large water and common sources
Note the mufta bihi measure for large stagnant water (10x10 cubits). Understand that water in containers (حب), cisterns (حوض), and wells (بئر) is presumed pure; one is not obligated to ask or investigate when impurity is uncertain.
This applies as long as one does not know (يعلم) or become certain of impurity.
3
Analyze the criteria for flowing water
Flowing water (جاري) becomes impure only if its taste, color, or smell changes due to impurity, indicating the actual presence of impurity. If no change occurs, it remains pure.
This is in contrast to stagnant water, which may be affected by a small impurity if below the minimum measure.
4
Understand the fifth type – water doubtful in purifying ability
The fifth type is water that is pure in itself (tahir) but its ability to purify (tahuriyya) is doubtful. The example: water drunk by a donkey or mule whose mother is a domestic donkey (not a mare). Such water can be used for drinking but not for wudu.
The ruling depends on the mother: if the mother is a mare (wild), the water remains purifying.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
توسعة على الناس، والتقدير بعشر في عشر هو المفتى به ولا بأس بالوضوء والشرب من حب يوضع كوزه في نواحي الدار ما لم يعلم تنجسه، ومن حوض يخاف أن يكون فيه قذر، ولا يتيقن ولا يجب أن يسأل عنه، ومن البئر التي تدلى فيها الدلاء، والجرار الدنسة، وتحملها الصغار والإماء ويمسها الرستاقيون بأيد دنسة ما لم تتيقن النجاسة (أو) كان ( جارياً) عطف على راكداً وظهر فيه أي الجاري (أثرها) فيكون نجساً (والأثر طعم) النجاسة (أو لون أو ريح لها وجود عين النجاسة بأثرها (و) النوع (الخامس ماء مشكوك في طهوريته لا في طهارته وهو ما شرب منه حمار أو بغل) وكانت أمه أتانا لا رمكة لأن العبرة للام كما سنذكره في الأسآر إن شاء الله تعالى
Relief for people, and the estimation of ten by ten is the relied upon position. There is no harm in performing ablution and drinking from a container placed in the corner of the house as long as one does not know it is impure, and from a cistern that one fears may contain impurity but is not certain, and one is not obligated to ask about it, and from a well into which buckets and dirty jars are lowered, and small children and maids carry them, and villagers touch them with dirty hands, as long as one is not certain of impurity. Or if it is flowing – as an alternative to stagnant – and its effect appears in it, then it is impure. The effect is taste, color, or smell of impurity, indicating the presence of the actual impurity. And the fifth type is water doubtful in its purifying ability but not in its purity, which is that from which a donkey or mule drank, and its mother is a domestic donkey, not a mare, because the consideration is the mother, as we will mention in the section on leftover water, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya provides practical rulings on water when impurity is uncertain. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the minimum measure for large water is ten by ten cubits. Water in containers, wells, and cisterns is considered pure unless impurity is certain; one need not ask about it. Flowing water becomes impure only if taste, color, or smell changes, indicating actual impurity. The fifth type is water drunk by a donkey or mule, which is pure in itself but doubtful in purifying ability; the ruling depends on the mother being a domestic donkey (not a mare).

Key Terms
راكد (rakid): Stagnant water that does not flow.
جاري (jari): Flowing water that does not become impure unless its attributes change.
ماء مشكوك في طهوريته (ma' mashkuk fi tahuriyyatih): Water whose ability to purify is doubtful but is still pure in itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Five by five cubits
B) Ten by ten cubits
C) Twenty by twenty cubits
D) Forty by forty cubits

Key Takeaway
Water is presumed pure until certainty of impurity; flowing water must show a change; water from a donkey or mule is pure but not purifying, with the ruling depending on the mother.

The Ruling on Human Su'r (Leftover Water)
Defines su'r and explains the first category (human) with proof and intra-madhhab difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on human su'r, explain the proof from the hadith of Aisha, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad when the mouth is impure.

Core Idea
Human leftover water is pure and purifying — even from a menstruating woman — but caution is required if the mouth was unclean.

Leftover water (su'r) is a key concept in Hanafi taharah. This lesson defines human su'r, establishes its default purity with a strong hadith proof, and then examines an important intra-madhhab difference when the person's mouth was impure. Understanding this will help you apply the correct ruling in daily acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Define su'r and its scope
Note that su'r applies only to small water (less than 10x10 cubits and not flowing). Learn the linguistic derivation.
The term is specific to leftover water; leftovers of other things are called by a different name.
2
Identify the default ruling for human su'r
Human su'r is unanimously pure (tahir) and purifying (mutahhir) without dislike. Understand the categories of humans included.
No distinction is made between Muslim/kafir, adult/child, or whether the person is in a state of impurity.
3
Analyse the hadith proof
The hadith of Aisha (ra) shows the Prophet (saw) drinking from the same cup after her while she was menstruating. This proves that her leftover water was pure and that her state did not affect the water.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim, a sound source.
4
Examine the intra-madhhab difference
When the person's mouth is impure (e.g., from alcohol, impure food), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that if the person clears the mouth by moving saliva and spitting/swallowing, the leftover is pure but disliked. Imam Muhammad holds it remains impure.
The difference is based on whether saliva removes impurity.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative position)
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: pure but makruh tanzihan. Avoid using such water in wudu/ghusl if other water is available.
This reflects caution despite the default purity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان أحكام السؤر) (والماء القليل) الذي بينا قدره بدون عشر في عشر ولم يكن جارياً إذا شرب منه حيوان يكون على أحد (أربعة أقسام و ما أبقاه بعد شربه (يسمى سؤراً) بهمز عينه، ويستعار الاسم لبقية الطعام، والجمع أسار والفعل أسأر أي أبقى شيئاً مما شربه والنعت منه سار على غير قياس لأن قياسه مسئر، ونظيره أجبره، فهو جبار (الأول) من الأقسام سؤر (طاهر مطهر) بالإتفاق من غير كراهة في استعماله وهو ما شرب منه (آدمي ليس بفمه نجاسة لما روى مسلم عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت : كنت أشرب، وأنا حائض فأناوله النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيضع فاه على موضع في ولا فرق بين الكبير والصغير والمسلم والكافر والحائض والجنب، وإذا تنجس فمه فشرب الماء من فوره تنجس، وإن كان بعدما تردّد البزاق في فمه مرات وألقاه أو ابتلعه قبل الشرب فلا يكون سؤره نجساً عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف لكنه مكروه لقول محمد بعدم طهارة النجاسة بالبزاق عنده
A chapter on the rulings of leftover water (su'r). And the small water whose amount we mentioned as less than ten by ten and not flowing, when an animal drinks from it, it is one of four types, and what remains after its drinking is called su'r (with a hamza on its 'ayn), and the name is metaphorically used for leftover food. The plural is asar, and the verb as'ara means to leave something from what he drank, and the adjective saar is irregular because its analogical form is mus'ir. The first type: leftover water that is pure and purifying by agreement, without dislike in using it. It is what a human drinks from, provided there is no impurity in his mouth. Based on what Muslim narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): 'I used to drink while I was menstruating, then I would give the cup to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and he would place his mouth on the spot where I had put my mouth.' There is no difference between adult and child, Muslim and non-Muslim, menstruating woman and person in major impurity. If his mouth becomes impure, then if he drinks immediately, his leftover is impure. But if after moving saliva in his mouth several times and spitting it out or swallowing it before drinking, then his leftover is not impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but it is disliked (makruh) due to Muhammad's statement that impurity is not removed by saliva.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on su'r (leftover water). Su'r is defined as the water left after a human or animal drinks from a small amount of water (less than 10x10 cubits and not flowing). The first of four categories is human su'r, which is unanimously pure and purifying without any dislike. The proof is the hadith of Aisha showing the Prophet drinking from her leftover while she was menstruating, indicating purity. The ruling applies to all humans regardless of age, faith, or state of ritual impurity. However, if the person's mouth is impure (e.g., from drinking alcohol, eating impure food, or vomiting), there is an intra-madhhab difference: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that if the person first clears his mouth by moving saliva around and then spitting or swallowing, the leftover is not impure, though it is disliked (makruh tanzihan) out of caution. Imam Muhammad holds that the impurity is not removed by saliva alone, so the leftover remains impure. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, with the dislike mentioned.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water after a human or animal drinks from a small amount of water (less than 10x10 cubits and not flowing).
طاهر مطهر (tahir mutahhir): Pure in itself and purifying for others (used to remove ritual impurity).
بزاق (buzq): Saliva; used in the context of clearing the mouth of impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on human leftover water if the person's mouth was impure but he cleared it by moving saliva and spitting before drinking?
A) Impure according to all scholars
B) Pure and purifying with no dislike
C) Pure but disliked according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
D) Impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf

Key Takeaway
Human leftover water from a small source is pure and purifying by default; caution applies only if the mouth was impure and even then, the relied-upon view declares it pure but disliked.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
7 min
Rulings on Leftover Water of Horses and Halal-Meat Animals
Covers the second and third categories of su'r with proofs and differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the su'r of a horse and explain why it is pure despite the dispute about its meat, and identify the condition for the su'r of halal-meat animals to be without dislike.

Core Idea
Horse su'r is pure and purifying; the dispute over horse meat does not affect its leftover water.

In this lesson, we continue the classification of su'r (leftover water). We will examine the second category: the leftover of a horse, and the third category: animals whose meat is halal. You'll learn that the horse's leftover is pure by consensus, even though its meat is subject to scholarly difference. For halal-meat animals, their leftover is pure and without dislike unless they are jallalah—animals that primarily consume filth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon (su'r of horse, su'r of halal-meat animals) and the initial hukm (purity).
Focus on the final ruling: pure and purifying.
2
Locate the dalil for horse su'r purity
Trace the reasoning: for Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, because horse meat is halal; for Abu Hanifa, because saliva is derived from pure flesh, and the prohibition of horse meat is for honor not impurity.
The proof is dalil aqli (rational) based on the nature of the animal.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on horse meat
Note that Abu Hanifa initially held horse meat haram but retracted; the final view is makruh tanzihan. This dispute does not affect the purity of su'r.
The retraction and fatwa establish the relied-upon position.
4
Apply the ruling to halal-meat animals
Camels, cows, sheep, and by extension birds: their su'r is pure and without dislike.
The reason: their saliva is from pure flesh.
5
Note the exception of jallalah
If the animal is a jallalah (habitually eats filth), its su'r becomes makruh (disliked) but remains pure.
This is a condition that changes the ruling level from mubah to makruh tanzihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو شرب منه (فرس) فإن سؤر الفرس طاهر بالإتفاق على الصحيح من غير كراهة (أو) شرب منه (ما) بمعنى حيوان (يؤكل لحمه) كالإبل، والبقر والغنم ولا كراهة في سؤرها إن لم تكن جلالة تأكل الجلة بالفتح وهي في أسار كنور، وأنوار مصباح قوله : ( لبقية الطعام الذي في المستصفى، والقهستاني عن المغرب أنه استعير لمطلق البقية من كل شيء قوله : ( والفعل أسأر ) يقال أسأر كأكرم وسأر كمنع إذا أبقى، وعقب كما في القاموس ويقال إذا شربت فأستر كأكرم قوله : (أي أبقى شيئاً مما شربه) لا حاجة إليه قوله : (والنعت منه سآر بوزن خطاب قوله : (لأن قياسه مستر) إلا انه لم يسمع كما صرح به أهل اللغة خلافاً للمجد في القاموس فجوّز القياس قوله: (وإذا تنجس فمه) كان شرب خمراً أو أكل أو شرب نجساً أو قاء ملء الفم قوله فلا يكون سؤره نجساً) ما لم يكن شاربه طويلاً لا يستوعبه اللسان، فسوره ،نجس، ولو بعد زمان كما في شرح التنوير . أمته، وكذا تنبيه : يكره أن يشرب سؤر غيره إن وجد منه لذة إلا الزوجين والسيد . يكره حلاقة الأمر إن وجد المحلوق رأسه من اللذة ما يزيد على ما لو كان الحلاق ملتحياً، وبالأولى كراهة تكبيس الأمرد في الحمام بالشرط المذكور قوله : لكنه مكروه) أي تنزيهاً مراعاة للخلاف قوله: (أو شرب منه فرس) لفظه يقع على الذكر والأنثى، وربما قالوا للأنثى فرسة قوله: (فإن سؤر الفرس طاهر بالاتفاق أما عندهما فظاهر لأنه مأكول عندهما، وأما عند الإمام فلان لعابه متولد من لحمه وهو طاهر وحرمته للتكريم لكونه آلة الجهاد فصارت حرمته كحرمة لحم الآدمي ألا : تری أن لبنه حلال بالإجماع، كما في التبيين بل صح رجوعه عن القول بحرمته قبل موته بثلاثة أيام وعليه الفتوى وذكر شيخ الإسلام، وغيره إن أكل لحمه مكروه وتنزيهاً في ظاهر الزاوية، وهو الصحيح كما في مجمع الأنهر قوله : على الصحيح) وقيل نجس حكاه صاحب منية المصلي، وقيل مشكوك كسور الحمار قوله : (من غير كراهة) وروى الحسن عن الإمام أنه مكروه كلحمه قوله : (كالإبل والبقر ) أدخلت الكاف الطيور مأكولة اللحم قوله: (ولا كراهة في سؤرها لأنه يتولد من لحم طاهر فأخذ حكمه قوله : إن لم تكن حلالاً تأكل الجلة)
Or if a horse drinks from it, then the leftover of the horse is pure by agreement, on the correct view, without dislike. Or if an animal whose meat is eaten drinks from it, like camels, cows, and sheep, and there is no dislike in their leftover, unless they are jallalah (eating filth). ... [linguistic notes] ... The leftover of a horse is pure by agreement: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad it is clear because it is eatable meat; according to Abu Hanifa, its saliva is generated from its flesh which is pure, and its prohibition is out of honor for being an instrument of jihad, so its forbiddenness is like that of human flesh. Indeed, its milk is halal by consensus. It is established that Abu Hanifa retracted his statement of prohibition three days before his death, and that is the fatwa. Sheikh al-Islam and others said that eating its meat is makruh tanzihan in the apparent view, and that is correct. ... The dislike in their leftover is because it is generated from pure flesh so it takes its ruling. The condition is that they are not jallalah eating filth.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage covers the second and third categories of su'r. The second category is the leftover of a horse. It is pure and purifying by agreement, and there is no dislike in using it. The text notes that some earlier opinions considered horse meat haram, but Abu Hanifa retracted that view, and the fatwa is that it is makruh tanzihan (recommendably disliked). The leftover, however, remains pure. The third category is the leftover of animals whose meat is halal (like camels, cows, sheep, and by extension, birds). Their leftover is also pure without dislike, provided they are not jallalah (animals that eat filth). If they are jallalah, their leftover may be disliked because the filth affects their saliva or milk. The passage also includes a note: it is disliked to drink another's leftover if it brings pleasure, except between spouses and master-slave. This highlights that the ruling of su'r is not just about ritual purity but also about etiquette.

Key Terms
جلالة (jallalah): An animal that primarily eats filth; its leftover, milk, and meat may be affected.
فرس (faras): Horse; both male and female.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition must be met for the leftover of halal-meat animals (like camels and cows) to be pure without dislike?
A) The animal must be a horse
B) The animal must not be a jallalah
C) The animal must be slaughtered properly
D) The animal must be an adult

Key Takeaway
Horse su'r is pure and purifying; halal-meat animal su'r is pure unless the animal is a jallalah, in which case it becomes disliked but remains pure.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
The Three Categories of Su'ur (Residual Water) in Hanafi Fiqh
Classifies su'ur according to animal mouth and meat purity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any su'ur into the correct category (pure, impure, or disliked) and state the supporting evidence from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Su'ur is ruled by the animal's mouth and flesh: pure from humans and halal animals, impure from dogs/pigs/predators, disliked from cats and jallalah.

In Hanafi taharah, leftover water (su'ur) after drinking is not all the same. Its legal status depends entirely on the source. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah provides a clear threefold classification, each supported by textual evidence. Understanding these categories is essential for ensuring the validity of wudu and avoiding contamination.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
From the passage, list the three categories of su'ur: pure and purifying (tahir mutahhir), impure (najis), and disliked (makruh).
2
Note the animals and conditions for each
For the first category: humans with pure mouths, horses, and halal meat animals that are not jallalah. For the second: dog, pig, and predatory beasts. For the third: domestic cat and jallalah animals.
The cat's su'ur is pure by ijma but disliked for purification – an important nuance.
3
Examine the proofs
The passage cites a hadith from Aisha (human su'ur), hadith from Daraqutni (dog su'ur), Quran verse for pig, and hadith about the cat 'tawwafin'. Identify each proof and how it supports the ruling.
For cat, the cause (illah) of 'tawwaf' removes impurity but not dislike.
4
Recognize intra-madhhab differences
Note the ikhtilaf: Imam Muhammad considers su'ur from a human with mouth impurity impure (others say pure but makruh); Abu Yusuf holds no dislike for cat su'ur.
The mufta bihi is the majority view: human su'ur is pure, cat su'ur is makruh tanzih.
5
Apply the classification
Given a specific animal (e.g., goat, wolf, pigeon, cat), determine its su'ur category and state whether it can be used for wudu.
Consider conditions like jallalah status and mouth impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

شرب منه (آدمي ليس بفمه نجاسة لما روى مسلم عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت : كنت أشرب، وأنا حائض فأناوله النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيضع فاه على موضع في ولا فرق بين الكبير والصغير والمسلم والكافر والحائض وهي في الأصل البعرة وقد يكنى بها عن العذرة فإن كانت جلالة فسؤرها من القسم الثالث مكروه (و) القسم (الثاني) سؤر (نجس) نجاسة غليظة وقيل خفيفة (لا يجوز استعماله) أي لا يصح التطهير به بحال، ولا يشربه إلا مضطرّ كالميتة (وهو) أي السؤر النجس (ما شرب منه الكلب) سواء فيه كلب صيد، وماشية وغيره لما روى الدارقطني عن أبي هريرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في الكلب بلغ في الإناء أنه يغسل ثلاثاً أو خمساً، أو سبعاً (أو) شرب منه (الخنزير) لنجاسة عينه لقوله تعالى: (فإنه رجس (أو) شرب منه (شيء) بمعنى حيوان من سباع البهائم احترز به عن سباع الطير وسيأتي حكمها، والسبع حيوان مختطف منتهب عادي عادة كالفهد والذئب)، سؤرها كما في الجوهرة قوله: (وقد يكنى بها عن العذرة) بكسر الذال ولا تسكن غائط بني آدم والعذرة اسم لفناء الدار، وكانوا يلقونها فيه فسميت باسم ظرفها قوله : (وقيل خفيفة محل الخلاف في غير الكلب، والخنزير لما أن المعتمد فيه أنه طاهر العين قوله : من سباع البهائم) سميت بهائم لانبهام الأمر عليها أو لانبهام أمرها علينا قوله: (وسيأتي حكمها أي في القسم الثالث قوله : (مختطف) لفظه يفيد السرعة بخلاف المنتهب Book of Purification. Food, and the plural is asar, and the verb is as'ara meaning he left something from what he drank, and the adjective is sa'ar on an irregular pattern because its regular pattern would be mus'ir. Its parallel is ajbarahu, so he is jabbar. (The first) of the categories is su'ur (which is pure and purifying) by agreement without dislike in its use, and it is what was drunk from (a human who has no impurity on his mouth) because of what Muslim narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: I used to drink while I was menstruating, then I would hand it to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and he would place his mouth at the spot where I placed my mouth. There is no difference between an adult and a child, a Muslim and a disbeliever, a menstruating woman and a person in major impurity. If his mouth becomes impure and he drinks water immediately, it becomes impure. But if the saliva circulated in his mouth several times and he expels it or swallows it before drinking, then his su'ur is not impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but it is disliked (makruh) because of Muhammad's statement that impurity is not removed by saliva according to him. (Or) a (horse) drank from it, for the su'ur of a horse is pure by agreement on the correct view without dislike. (Or) (an animal whose meat is eaten) drank from it, such as camels, cows, and sheep, and there is no dislike in their su'ur if they are not jallalah that eat jallah (dung). Jallah, with a fatha, is originally a camel dropping, and it can be used metaphorically for human waste. If it is a jallalah, then its su'ur is from the third category, disliked. (And) the (second) category is su'ur (impure) with severe impurity, and it is said light impurity, (use of which is not permissible), i.e., purification with it is not valid at all, and it should not be drunk except by one forced like carrion. (It is) the impure su'ur (what the dog drank from), whether a hunting dog, livestock dog, or other, because of what al-Daraqutni narrated from Abu Huraira from the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding the dog's lapping in the vessel: that it should be washed three, five, or seven times. (Or) the (pig) drank from it, due to the impurity of its essence because of His statement (so it is an abomination). (Or) (something) meaning an animal from the predatory beasts drank from it, with the reservation of predatory birds, whose ruling will come later. A prey animal is a predatory, attacking, aggressive creature by nature, like the leopard, wolf, hyena, tiger, lion, and monkey, because their saliva is generated from their flesh which is impure like their milk. (And) the (third) category is su'ur (whose use is disliked) in purification with a tanzih dislike, in the presence of other water that is not disliked, and it is not disliked when water is absent because it is pure and it is not permissible to resort to tayammum while it exists. (It is) the su'ur of the (domestic cat), due to the removal of the ruling of impurity by agreement, due to the cause of the circumambulation mentioned in his statement: 'It is not impure; it is among those who go around among you.' That is, only if it eats filth and most of its fodder is pure, then there is no dislike in its su'ur, as in al-Jawhara. He said: 'And it can be used metaphorically for human waste' with a kasra on the dhal, and it does not become sukun; it is the excrement of humans. Al-adhra is the name for the courtyard of the house, and they used to throw it there, so it was named after its container. He said: 'And it is said light impurity, the point of dispute is for other than the dog and pig; as for them, they are severe by agreement. Then the severity and lightness only appear in things that are not liquids.' He said: 'That is, purification with it is not valid' to ward off the misconception of meaning prohibition, and it is compatible with correctness as from his statement: 'And it should not be drunk except by one forced like carrion, but one should not drink from it nor eat from it except as much as sustains the body, as indicated by Allamah Nuh.' He said: 'That it should be washed three, etc.' That is only because of its impurity, and according to us, seven times is recommended, and one of them with earth. He said: 'The impurity of its essence' — he did not say the equivalent for the dog because the relied-upon view is that it is pure in essence. He said: 'From the predatory beasts' they are called beasts because the matter is hidden from them or because their matter is hidden from us. He said: 'And its ruling will come later, meaning in the third category.' He said: 'Rapid' — its wording indicates speed unlike al-muntahib. He said: 'In purification' — restricting it to purification indicates that there is no dislike in drinking and cooking, but that is not the case. He said: 'A tanzih dislike' — what he mentioned is the correct view, while Abu Yusuf held that the su'ur of the cat is permissible to drink and perform wudu with without dislike. He said: 'And it is not disliked when water is absent' — the pronoun refers to the cat's su'ur. He said: 'By agreement' — the dispute is only about the dislike; indeed Abu Yusuf does not hold it as mentioned. He said: 'By the cause of circumambulation' — the idafah is for explanation. He said: 'Mentioned in the text' — it is mentioned with consideration of the addressee. He said: 'It is of those who go around you' — an explanation of the necessity that removes the ruling of impurity, and the feminine is with consideration of the word 'al-hirah' (cat), which is a generic noun encompassing male and female. 'Al-tawwafin' is a plural of males and females, and its plural is a plural of those who possess intellect, which is used for nearby things. He said in al-Qamus: the plural is 'al-tawwafat'.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi provides a detailed classification of su'ur (leftover water after drinking) into three categories. It begins with a lexical note on the word 'su'ur', then explains each category with its ruling and evidence.

First Category: Pure and Purifying Su'ur (Tahir Mutahhir)
The first category includes su'ur from a human whose mouth is free of impurity. The proof is the hadith of Aisha (ra) showing the Prophet (saw) drank from the same vessel she used while menstruating. This covers all humans regardless of age, faith, or ritual state. If the mouth is impure (e.g., from drinking wine or eating impurity), the su'ur becomes impure unless the person first circulates saliva and expels or swallows it before drinking. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the su'ur remains pure, but Imam Muhammad holds it impure because saliva does not remove impurity; hence the su'ur is considered makruh tanzih to respect the ikhtilaf. Su'ur from a horse is pure by consensus, though there is a weak view of impurity. The relied-upon position is that horse meat is permissible, contrary to earlier prohibition. Su'ur from animals whose meat is eaten (camel, cow, sheep, birds) is pure and not disliked, provided they are not jallalah (animals that habitually eat dung). If they are jallalah, their su'ur falls into the third category (makruh).

Second Category: Impure Su'ur (Najis)
The second category is su'ur that is impure and cannot be used for purification. This includes su'ur from a dog, pig, and predatory beasts (like wolf, leopard, hyena, etc.). For the dog, the proof is the hadith commanding washing the vessel three, five, or seven times due to its impurity. In the Hanafi school, seven washes are recommended (not obligatory), and one of them should be with earth (though not obligatory). The pig is impure in essence by Quranic text (al-An'am:145). Predatory beasts are included because their flesh is impure (their meat is not eaten), so their saliva is impure like their milk. Note that the dog's essence is considered pure in the relied-upon Hanafi view (unlike the pig), but its saliva is impure. Predatory birds are excluded and will be discussed later under the third category.

Third Category: Makruh Su'ur (Disliked)
The third category is su'ur that is disliked (makruh tanzih) to use for purification when other water is available. The primary example is the domestic cat. The cat's su'ur is pure by agreement (ijma) due to the hadith: 'It is not impure; it is among those who go around you.' However, Abu Yusuf holds that it is not disliked at all, while the correct position is that it is makruh tanzih out of caution. This dislike applies only to using it for purification, not for drinking or cooking. If no other water is available, it is not disliked because one cannot resort to tayammum while pure water exists. Additionally, animals whose meat is eaten but become jallalah (habitually eating filth) also fall into this category: their su'ur is makruh until they are confined for a period (istibra') and their meat becomes pure.

The commentary also clarifies various nuanced points: the distinction between severe and light impurity applies only to non-liquids; the dog's essence is not impure but its saliva is; and the term 'jallah' is a metaphor for human waste. The overall structure follows the three-fold division, each supported by textual evidence and intra-madhhab discussions.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'ur): The remaining water left in a vessel after a person or animal has drunk from it.
طاهر مطهر (tahir mutahhir): Pure in itself and capable of purifying other things (used for wudu/ghusl).
جلالة (jallalah): An animal that habitually eats impure substances (dung, filth) such that its meat and milk are affected.
مكروه تنزيه (makruh tanzih): Disliked but not prohibited; omitting it is better than doing it, but doing it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on su'ur (leftover water) from a domestic cat?
A) It is pure (tahir) and allowed for purification without any dislike.
B) It is impure (najis) and cannot be used for purification.
C) It is pure but disliked (makruh tanzih) to use for purification when other water is available.
D) It is prohibited (haram) to use for purification under any circumstance.

Key Takeaway
Su'ur is categorized by source: pure from humans and halal animals (non-jallalah), impure from dogs/pigs/predatory beasts, and disliked from cats and jallalah animals.

Impure Su'r: Dog, Pig, and Predatory Beasts
Defines the second category of residual water - impure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of impure su'r according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence and severity for each.

Core Idea
Su'r of dogs, pigs, and predatory beasts is impure and invalid for purification.

This lesson addresses a practical question: can you perform wudu with water left after a dog drinks? The answer is no — it falls under the second category of residual water: impure. We will explore the rulings for dogs, pigs, and predatory beasts, the evidence from Quran and Hadith, and why the dog's saliva is impure despite its body being pure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that the passage defines the second category of su'r: impure (najis). This is distinct from pure su'r (e.g., cat, horse) and disliked su'r (e.g., chicken).
The three-category classification is unique to the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the ruling for each animal
Note that the su'r of a dog, pig, and any predatory beast (like leopard, wolf, hyena, tiger, lion, monkey) is impure. The dog includes all types (hunting, livestock, etc.).
The pig's impurity is from its essence (Quran), while the dog's impurity is from its saliva (Hadith).
3
Analyse the evidence
For the dog: the Hadith commanding washing the vessel three, five, or seven times indicates impurity. For the pig: the Quran calls it 'rijis'. For beasts: analogy (qiyas) based on the impurity of their flesh and milk, since saliva originates from flesh.
The hadith is ahad, so it provides zanni thubut, but it is accepted by the school.
4
Distinguish severity
Note the intra-Hanafi difference: some say the impurity of predatory beasts is light (khafif), but the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that it is severe (ghaliz), like the dog and pig. Understand the practical consequence: severe impurity requires washing three times, once with earth (for dog), while light impurity requires only one wash.
The distinction between severe and light impurity affects the method of purification.
5
Refine the concept
The commentator refines a potential misunderstanding: the ruling 'use is not permissible' refers to validity of purification, not general permissibility. Also, the dog's body is pure in essence; only its saliva is impure.
This refinement shows the depth of Hanafi legal analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the second category: residual water that is impure, with severe impurity, and it is said light impurity. Its use is not permissible, meaning purification with it is not valid at all, and only a person in dire need may drink it, like carrion. And it is the impure residual water from which a dog has drunk, whether it is a hunting dog, livestock dog, or other, due to what al-Daraqutni narrated from Abu Hurairah from the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding a dog licking in a vessel, that it should be washed three times, or five, or seven. Or if a pig has drunk from it, due to the impurity of its essence, because Allah says: 'It is an abomination.' Or if something, meaning an animal from among the predatory beasts, from which he excluded predatory birds, and their ruling will come later. And a predatory beast is an animal that snatches and plunders, normally aggressive, like the leopard and wolf, and the hyena, tiger, lion, and monkey, because their saliva originates from their flesh, which is impure, like their milk. His saying: 'i.e., purification is not valid' repels the misunderstanding of intending non-permissibility; and it is compatible with validity, as from his saying: 'And only a person in dire need may drink it, like carrion' but he may not drink from it nor eat from it except the amount that sustains the body, as taught by Allamah Nooh. His saying: 'That it is washed three times etc.' and that is only due to its impurity, and according to us, seven times is recommended, and one of them with earth. His saying: 'The impurity of its essence' – he did not say the same regarding the dog because the relied-upon view is that it is pure in essence. His saying: 'From among the predatory beasts' they are called beasts because their matter is ambiguous to them, or because their matter is ambiguous to us. His saying: 'And their ruling will come later' i.e., in the third section. His saying: 'snatches' its wording indicates speed, unlike 'plunders'.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage from the hashiya defines the second category of residual water (su'r), which is impure (najis). The matn states that the su'r of a dog, pig, and any predatory beast is impure. The commentary refines this by clarifying that the prohibition of use is not about permissibility but about legal purity for worship. The dog's su'r is impure due to the hadith commanding washing the vessel three, five, or seven times, with one using earth. The pig's su'r is impure because the Quran calls it 'rijis' (abomination). For predatory beasts like leopard, wolf, hyena, tiger, lion, and monkey, their saliva is impure because it originates from their flesh, which is impure (like their milk). The commentator notes a difference of opinion regarding the severity: some say it is severe impurity (najis ghaliz), others light (najis khafif). The relied-upon view is that the dog and pig are severe, while other beasts are considered impure but with some leniency. The commentary also notes that the impurity of the dog is not from its essence (the dog itself is pure in essence according to the Hanafi school), but from its saliva due to the hadith. This distinction is important: the dog's body is pure, but its saliva is impure.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The residual water left in a vessel after an animal drinks from it, or the leftover water after drinking.
نجاسة غليظة (najasah ghalizah): Severe impurity that requires special purification, like washing with earth for dogs.
سباع البهائم (siba' al-baha'im): Predatory beasts, large animals that hunt and plunder, such as leopard, wolf, hyena, tiger, lion, and monkey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason for the impurity of the pig's su'r as opposed to the dog's?
A) The dog is impure in essence, while the pig is not
B) The pig is impure in essence (najis al-ayn) by Quran, while the dog's impurity is based on a hadith regarding its saliva
C) The pig's su'r is less severe than the dog's
D) The pig's su'r is pure but disliked

Key Takeaway
The su'r of dogs, pigs, and predatory beasts is impure (najis) and cannot be used for purification, with the dog's impurity based on hadith, the pig's on Quran, and predators' on analogy.

The Ruling on Cat's Su'r: Pure but Disliked
Definition of the third category of su'r

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the household cat's su'r, explain the reason for its dislike, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Cat's su'r is pure but disliked for purification when other water exists.

This passage addresses a common question: is the leftover water of a household cat pure or impure? The Hanafi school, based on a prophetic hadith, declares it pure but adds a layer of dislike (karahah tanzih) due to the cat's daily habits. We will examine the evidence, the reasoning behind the dislike, and the alternative view of Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling category
Determine what is being ruled upon: the su'r (residual water) of the domestic cat. Note that it falls into the third category of su'r: disliked.
The first two categories are pure (tahir) and impure (najis).
2
Understand the legal cause (illa)
The reason the cat's su'r is not impure is the hadith: the cat is among those who 'go around you' (tawwafin). This domestic proximity lifts impurity.
This ʿilla is specific to domestic cats; wild cats do not share this ruling.
3
Trace the dislike
Despite purity, the use of this water is disliked (makruh tanzih) when other water is available. Why? Because cats do not avoid impurities, so there is a possibility of contamination.
This dislike is precautionary, not based on inherent filth.
4
Compare with Abu Yusuf's view
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that cat's su'r is completely permissible without any dislike, citing the literal hadith. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is the slight dislike, as stated by the author.
The practical difference is mainly the merit of avoiding such water when possible.

And the third category: residual water (whose use is disliked) in purification, with a tanzihi (lesser) dislike, when there is other water without dislike. It is not disliked when there is no water because it is pure; one may not resort to tayammum when it is present. And it is the residual water of the household cat, because the ruling of impurity is dropped by agreement, due to the reason of 'tawwaf' (going around) mentioned in the hadith: 'It is not impure; it is among those who go around you.' That is, only if it mixes and most of its feed is pure, then there is no dislike in its su'r, as in al-Jawharah. His saying: 'And it may be a metaphor for stool' – with kasr of dhal, not sukun, meaning human excrement. 'Adhirah' is the name for the courtyard of a house, and they used to throw it there, so it was named after its container. His saying: 'And it is said light impurity' – the place of difference is other than dog and pig; as for those, they are severe by agreement. Then severity and lightness appear only in liquids. His saying: 'i.e., purification is not valid' repels the misunderstanding of intending non-permissibility; and it is compatible with validity, as from his saying: 'And only a person in dire need may drink it, like carrion' but he may not drink from it nor eat from it except the amount that sustains the body, as taught by Allamah Nooh. His saying: 'That it is washed three times etc.' and that is only due to its impurity, and according to us, seven times is recommended, and one of them with earth. His saying: 'The impurity of its essence' – he did not say the same regarding the dog because the relied-upon view is that it is pure in essence. His saying: 'From among the predatory beasts' they are called beasts because their matter is ambiguous to them, or because their matter is ambiguous to us. His saying: 'And their ruling will come later' i.e., in the third section. His saying: 'snatches' its wording indicates speed, unlike 'plunders'. His saying: 'in purification' – restricting it to purification indicates that it is not disliked for drinking and cooking, but it is not like that. His saying: 'dislike of tanzih' – what he mentioned is correct, and Abu Yusuf went that the cat's su'r is permissible to drink and perform wudu with without dislike. His saying: 'And it is not disliked when there is no water' – the pronoun refers to what? His saying: 'by agreement' – the difference is only in dislike, for Abu Yusuf does not say it as passed. His saying: 'due to the reason of tawwaf' – the addition is for explanation. His saying: 'what is mentioned in the text' – it is mentioned with consideration of the mudaf ilayhi. His saying: 'It is among those who go around you' – an explanation of the necessity that drops the ruling of impurity; the feminine is with consideration of the word 'cat', which is a generic noun covering male and female, and 'tawwafin' is the plural of males? and females? and its plural is the plural of those who are intelligent? Those who are in proximity to those who are intelligent. Al-Qamus said: plural and tawwafat. Al-Tirmidhi said: hasan sahih hadith, but its su'r is disliked as tanzih according to the most correct view, because it does not avoid impurity, like water in which a child has dipped his hand. And the Prophet's allowing the cat to drink from the vessel is interpreted as removing that doubt because of its condition in a time when the impurity of its mouth by something impure it ingested was not imagined. The su'r of a wild cat is impure due to the absence of the reason of tawwaf. And it is disliked for a cat to lick a person's hand, then he prays before washing it, or eats the leftover of what it ate, if he is rich and finds other, and it is not disliked for the poor out of necessity. His saying: 'And it is disliked for a cat to lick' etc. is restricted to a state of doubt; if the doubt is removed, there is no dislike. Similarly, regarding eating and drinking its su'r, as researched by al-Kamal. His saying: 'out of necessity' – he indicates that he found no other, and to the rich it is disliked, so there is no difference, as mentioned by some of the skillful.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of su'r: the residual water of the household cat is disliked (makruh tanzihan) for use in purification. The dislike is only when other water without dislike is available; if no water is found, it is not disliked because the water is pure and one cannot perform tayammum when pure water exists. The reason the cat's su'r is not impure is the prophetic hadith: 'It is not impure; it is among those who go around you' (tawwafin). This 'tawwaf' is the reason for dropping impurity, as cats are domestic animals that go around the house. The commentator notes that this is agreed upon, but there is a difference of opinion regarding dislike: Imam Abu Yusuf holds that there is no dislike at all, while the relied-upon view (al-sahih) is that it is mildly disliked (tanzih) because cats do not avoid impurity. The su'r of a wild cat, however, is impure because it lacks the reason of tawwaf. Additional rulings: it is disliked for a cat to lick a person's hand before he washes it, but if the person is poor (finds no other food), it is not disliked to eat the leftover. The commentary emphasizes that the dislike is based on the possibility of impurity; if one is certain the cat's mouth was clean, there is no dislike.

Key Terms
طواف (tawwaf): Literally 'going around'; in this context, it refers to the cat's habit of moving around the house and being in close proximity to humans, which is the reason for the lifting of impurity.
كراهة تنزيه (karahah tanzih): A less severe dislike, meaning the act is closer to permissible than to forbidden; it is not sinful to do it, but avoiding it is better.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is impure (najis) and cannot be used
B) It is pure and recommended
C) It is disliked (makruh tanzihan) when other water is available
D) It is forbidden (haram) to use

Key Takeaway
The household cat's su'r is pure in essence but mildly disliked for purification when alternative water exists, reflecting the Hanafi balance between evidence and precaution.

Su'r of Chicken and Jallalah Animals: From Dislike to Purity
Ruling on su'r of chicken and jallalah animals with confinement periods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the su'r of a free-roaming chicken (mukhalla) versus a confined chicken, and apply the confinement periods for jallalah animals to determine when their products become permissible.

Core Idea
The su'r of a mukhalla chicken is disliked due to doubt; confinement removes it, and jallalah animals require specific periods to become pure.

In this lesson, we examine the detailed rulings on the leftover water (su'r) of chickens, specifically distinguishing between confined and free-roaming birds. The passage also extends these principles to jallalah animals—those that feed on filth—and defines the confinement periods that purify their milk and meat. Understanding these distinctions prevents overgeneralization and ensures proper application in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The passage first rules on the su'r of chicken. The default ruling for a free-roaming chicken (mukhalla) is that its su'r is makruh tanzih due to the unknown purity of its beak.
The dislike is due to doubt, not certainty.
2
Identify the exception
If the chicken is confined in a clean environment so its beak does not touch filth, then its su'r is not disliked. The dislike is removed when the condition (unknown purity) is absent.
The commentator emphasizes that the ruling depends on the situation of the chicken.
3
Extend to jallalah animals
The same principle of dislike due to impurity extends to jallalah animals (camels, cows, sheep that feed on filth). Their milk and meat are disliked if they have a foul odor.
The sweat of jallalah is considered pure on the apparent view.
4
Apply the confinement periods
To remove the dislike, the animal must be confined and fed clean food until the foul odor disappears. The period is estimated by istihsan: 3 days for chicken, 4 for sheep, 10 for camels/cows.
These periods are based on istihsan, not a direct textual proof.
5
Note the critical refinement
The commentator critiques the author's wording, stating that the ruling for mukhalla could be derived without explicit mention. He also clarifies that the su'r of a mukhalla is disliked only when the beak's purity is unknown; if known impure, it is impure by consensus.
This refinement prevents misunderstanding that all chicken su'r is disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) سؤر (الدجاجة) بتثليث الدال وتاؤها للوحدة لا للتأنيث والدجاج مشترك بين الذكر والأنثى والدجاجة الأنثى خاصة، ولهذا لو حلف لا يأكل لحم دجاجة لا يحنث بلحم الديك ويكره سؤر (المخلاة) التي تجول في القاذورات ولم يعلم طهارة منقارها من نجاسته فكره سؤرها للشك فإن لم يكن كذلك فلا كراهة فيه بأن حبست فلا يصل منقارها لقذر قوله: (والدجاج مشترك) ويفرق بينه وبين واحده بالتاء كتمر وتمرة وبيض وبيضة قوله : ( والدجاجة الأنثى خاصة هذا اصطلاح الفقهاء بدليل ما بعده وهذا من المصنف خلط اصطلاح بلغة فأوقع في الوهم قوله: (ويكره سور المخلاة لا حاجة إلى هذه الزيادة والمخلاة بالخاء المعجمة وتشديد اللام المرسلة قال شيخ الإسلام، في مبسوطه هي التي لا تعلف في البيوت، فلا تتحامى النجاسات بواسطة التقاط الحب، فمنقارها لا يخلو عن قذر فتثبت الكراهة لاحتمال حتى لو تيقن ذلك عند شربها كان سؤرها نجساً اتفاقاً وأما محل الكراهة عند جهالة الحال برهان وكذا الحكم في إبل وبقر وغنم جلالة فالأولى حذف دجاجة وعرق الجلالة طاهر على الظاهر خالية وكره لبن الجلالة، ولحمها إذا أنتن وتحبس لتزول الكراهة حتى يذهب نتنه وقدر بثلاثة أيام للدجاجة، وللشاة بأربعة، وللإبل والبقر بعشرة در في الاستحسان قال الحموي والدجاج لا بأس به لأن لحمه لا يتغير أهـ. قوله : (التي تجول أي تطوف أو تدور أفاده في القاموس في جملة معان قوله : (ولم يعلم طهارة منقارها أما إذا علمت أو ضدها فالحكم ظاهر قوله : (بأن حبست الخ) الحبس كما قال شيخ الإسلام أن تحبس في بيت وتعلف هناك، فلا تجد عذرات غيرها حتى تفتش فيها الحب وهي لا تفتش في عذرات نفسها عادة فأمن تفتيش النجاسة اهـ قوله: اللزوم طوافها أي والطواف الذي هو العلة في هذا الباب لسقوط النجاسة في حقها الزم قوله :
And the residual water of the chicken – with three possible pronunciations of the daal, and its ta is for the unit, not for femininity. 'Dajaj' is common between male and female, and 'dajaja' specifically the female. Therefore, if someone swears not to eat the meat of a chicken (dajaja), he does not break the oath with the meat of a rooster. And the su'r of the mukhalla (free-roaming chicken) is disliked, which roams in filth and the purity of its beak is not known from impurity, so its su'r is disliked due to doubt. If it is not like that, then there is no dislike, i.e., if it is confined so its beak does not reach filth. His saying: 'Dajaj is common' – it is distinguished from its unit by the ta, like tamr/tamra, bayd/bayda. His saying: 'Dajaja specifically the female' – this is the terminology of the jurists, as shown by what follows, and the author mixed terminology with language, causing illusion. His saying: 'And the su'r of mukhalla is disliked' – there is no need for this addition. Mukhalla is with a kha with i'jam and tashdid of the lam. Shaikh al-Islam said in his Mabsut: it is that which is not fed in houses, so it does not avoid impurities by picking grains, so its beak is not free from filth, so dislike is established due to possibility, until if one is certain of that when drinking, its su'r is impure by agreement. The place of dislike is when the situation is unknown as proof. Similarly, the ruling for camels, cows, and sheep that are jallalah (eating filth). So it is better to delete chicken. The sweat of a jallalah animal is pure on the apparent view. And the milk of a jallalah is disliked, and its meat if it becomes putrid. And it is confined until the dislike is removed, until its stench goes away. It is estimated as three days for a chicken, four for a sheep, and ten for camels and cows by way of istihsan. Al-Hamawi said: Chicken is fine because its meat does not change. End. His saying: 'which roams' – meaning it goes around or circulates; al-Qamus gave that among meanings. His saying: 'and the purity of its beak is not known' – if it is known or the opposite, the ruling is apparent. His saying: 'if it is confined' – confinement, as Shaikh al-Islam said, is that it is confined in a house and fed there, so it does not find other droppings to search in, and it does not search in its own droppings by habit, so it is safe from searching impurity. His saying: 'the necessity of its tawwaf' – meaning the tawwaf which is the reason in this chapter for the removal of impurity in its case is necessary.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage discusses the su'r of chicken and the concept of mukhalla (free-roaming chicken) and jallalah (animals that eat filth). The su'r of a free-roaming chicken (mukhalla) is disliked because its beak may be contaminated from picking in filth. If the chicken is confined and its beak is known to be clean, there is no dislike. The commentator notes that the author's separation of chicken from mukhalla is redundant. The ruling for jallalah animals (camels, cows, sheep that feed on filth) is similar: their milk and meat are disliked if they have a foul odor. Confinement for a certain period (3 days for chicken, 4 for sheep, 10 for camels) removes the dislike. The sweat of a jallalah animal is considered pure. The last part references the concept of 'tawwaf' (going around) as the reason for dropping impurity, which was discussed earlier for cats. The passage ends mid-sentence on page 31, mentioning that the tawwaf is the reason in this chapter.

Key Terms
المخلاة (al-mukhalla): A free-roaming chicken that is not fed at home but picks up food from various places, so its beak may be contaminated.
الجلالة (al-jallalah): An animal that predominantly feeds on filth or impure things, causing its meat and milk to be affected.
الدجاج (al-dajaj): The generic term for chicken, common for both male and female.
الدجاجة (al-dajaja): Specifically a female chicken, as per the jurists' terminology.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many days of confinement are estimated for a jallalah cow to remove the dislike from its milk?
A) 3 days
B) 4 days
C) 10 days
D) 7 days

Key Takeaway
The dislike in su'r and jallalah products is contingent on doubt of impurity; confinement with clean food removes the doubt.

Sūr of Birds of Prey: Qiyas and Istihsān
Presents the ruling for sūr of birds of prey with qiyas and istihsān reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules the sūr of birds of prey as pure by istihsān, overriding the qiyas that would make it najis.

Core Idea
Birds of prey drink with a dry beak, so their sūr is pure by istihsān, unlike beasts of prey.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the Hanafi ruling on the residual water (sūr) of birds of prey. The author presents a qiyas (analogy) that would render it impure, but then applies istihsān (juristic preference) to declare it pure, based on the physical difference in how they drink. Understanding this reasoning is key to mastering Hanafi methodology in taharah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling by qiyas
Recognize that the analogy to beasts of prey would make the sūr of birds of prey najis, because their meat is haram and they consume impurities.
Beasts of prey have impure saliva that wets their tongue.
2
Identify the exception via istihsān
Note that the Hanafi school departs from qiyas due to a stronger consideration: birds drink with their beak, which is a hard, dry bone, not a moist tongue. Hence their sūr is ruled pure.
Istihsān is a valid source of law in the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the condition of certainty
The text adds that if one is certain the beak is free of impurity, the sūr is not even disliked. This shows the ruling is based on probability, not absolute impurity.
Certainty overrides the default dislike.
4
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Consider a falcon drinking from a bowl. Normally, the water is makrūh. But if you saw its beak was clean, the water is pure with no dislike.
This illustrates how practical knowledge changes the hukm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سؤر (سباع الطير كالصقر والشاهين والحدأة والرخم والغراب مكروه لأنها تخالط الميتات والنجاسات فأشبهت الدجاجة المخلاة حتى لو تيقن أنه لا نجاسة على منقارها لا يكره سؤرها، وكان القياس نجاسته لحرمة لحمها كسباع البهائم لكن طهارته استحسان لأنها تشرب بمنقارها، وهو عظم طاهر، وسباع البهائم تشرب بلسانها، وهو مبتل بلعابها النجس (و) سؤر (سواكن البيوت مما له دم سائل (كالفأرة)، والحية والوزعة مكروه للزوم طوافها، وحرمة لحمها النجس ، و (لا) كذلك سؤر (العقرب)، والخنفس، والصرصر لعدم نجاستها فلا كراهة فيه
The residual water (sūr) of birds of prey such as the falcon, eagle, kite, vulture, and crow is disliked (makrūh) because they mix with dead animals and impurities, thus resembling a free-roaming chicken. If one is certain that there is no impurity on its beak, its sūr is not disliked. The analogy (qiyās) would require it to be impure due to the prohibition of their meat, like beasts of prey, but its purity is by istihsān because they drink with their beak, which is a pure bone, while beasts of prey drink with their tongue, which is moist with their impure saliva. And the sūr of domestic animals that have flowing blood, such as the mouse, snake, and gecko, is disliked due to their constant roaming and the impurity of their forbidden meat. However, the sūr of the scorpion, beetle, and cricket is not like that, because they are not impure, so there is no dislike for their sūr.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya explains rulings for the sūr (residual water) of different animals. The author states the ruling for birds of prey: their sūr is makrūh (disliked) because they eat carrion and impurities. However, if one knows the beak is clean, it is not disliked. The qiyās would make it najis (impure) since their meat is haram, but istihsān gives purity because they drink with their beak (a dry bone) while beasts of prey drink with moist tongues that carry impurity. Next, domestic animals like mice and snakes have makrūh sūr due to their constant movement and impure meat. For insects like scorpions and beetles, no dislike exists because their bodies are not inherently impure. The reasoning combines direct rulings with istihsān based on physical differences.

Key Terms
سؤر (sūr): The water left in a vessel after an animal drinks from it.
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyās due to a stronger consideration (here, the dry beak).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the default ruling on the sūr of a falcon when its beak may be impure?
A) Najis (impure)
B) Makrūh (disliked)
C) Mubāh (permissible)
D) Harām (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsān to override qiyas for birds of prey, ruling their sūr pure but disliked unless the beak is known clean.

Sūr of Domestic Animals and Insects
Presents the ruling for sūr of domestic animals (mouse, snake, gecko) and insects (scorpion, beetle, cricket).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between animals whose sūr is makrūh and those whose sūr is not, based on blood flow and impurity.

Core Idea
Animals with flowing blood and impure meat have makrūh sūr; insects without that impurity have no dislike.

This lesson continues the Hashiya passage, covering the sūr of domestic animals like mice, snakes, and geckos, as well as insects like scorpions and beetles. The ruling hinges on whether the animal has flowing blood (damm sā'il) and whether its meat is impure. Understanding this distinction helps apply consistent rules in matters of taharah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of animals with flowing blood
The text lists mouse, snake, and gecko as examples of 'domestic animals with flowing blood' whose meat is impure and who roam constantly. Their sūr is ruled makrūh.
Flowing blood indicates a higher level of impurity compared to insects.
2
Identify the category of animals without flowing blood
Scorpions, beetles, and crickets are not considered impure (najis), so their sūr has no dislike (no karāhah).
These insects do not have flowing blood, so their bodies are not inherently impure.
3
Understand the reasoning for dislike
The dislike for the flowing-blood animals is due to their constant roaming in impure places and the impurity of their meat. This makes their saliva likely impure.
The ruling is based on probability, not certainty.
4
Apply the ruling to other similar animals
You can extend the ruling: any animal with flowing blood that lives in houses and eats impurities will have makrūh sūr. Animals without flowing blood (most insects) will have pure sūr without dislike.
This is a useful rule of thumb in fiqh al-taharah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The residual water (sūr) of birds of prey such as the falcon, eagle, kite, vulture, and crow is disliked (makrūh) because they mix with dead animals and impurities, thus resembling a free-roaming chicken. If one is certain that there is no impurity on its beak, its sūr is not disliked. However, the sūr of the scorpion, beetle, and cricket is not like that, because they are not impure, so there is no dislike for their sūr.

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya explains rulings for the sūr (residual water) of different animals. The author states the ruling for birds of prey: their sūr is makrūh (disliked) because they eat carrion and impurities. However, if one knows the beak is clean, it is not disliked. The qiyās would make it najis (impure) since their meat is haram, but istihsān gives purity because they drink with their beak (a dry bone) while beasts of prey drink with moist tongues that carry impurity. Next, domestic animals like mice and snakes have makrūh sūr due to their constant movement and impure meat. For insects like scorpions and beetles, no dislike exists because their bodies are not inherently impure. The reasoning combines direct rulings with istihsān based on physical differences.

Key Terms
دم سائل (dam sā'il): Flowing blood; blood that flows when an animal's skin is cut. Used as a criterion for impurity.
سواكن البيوت (sawākin al-buyūt): Domestic animals that live in and around houses, such as mice, snakes, and geckos.

B) Najis (impure)
C) No karāhah (not disliked)

Key Takeaway

The Doubtful Sūr (Sūr Mashkūk) and Its Ruling
Explains the doubtful sūr, its definition, and the ruling for donkey and mule sūr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the doubtful sūr and explain how conflicting proofs necessitate combining wudu and tayammum.

Core Idea
When water's purifying capacity is doubtful, combine wudu and tayammum for certainty.

In this passage, the Hashiya explains the fourth category of sūr: the doubtful sūr (sūr mashkūk). This term, introduced by later Hanafi scholars, refers to water whose purity is certain but whose capacity to remove ritual impurity (ṭahūriyyah) is uncertain due to conflicting evidences. The primary case is the sūr of donkey and mule, where conflicting hadith on the permissibility of their meat create doubt. The Hanafi solution is a precautionary combination: perform wudu with the doubtful water and then tayammum, ensuring valid purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that this passage deals with the fourth category of sūr: the doubtful sūr (sūr mashkūk). Note that this term is a later development, not found in early texts.
The category arises from conflicting evidence, not from essential impurity.
2
Analyze the conflicting proofs
Understand why the sūr of donkey and mule is doubtful: there are conflicting hadith on the permissibility of donkey meat (taʿāruḍ al-khabarayn). Additionally, the necessity of avoiding hardship (Ḥaraj) due to the donkey's constant contact with humans influences the ruling.
The doubt is in ṭahūriyyah, not in purity.
3
State the relied-upon ruling
According to al-Bahr, the sweat and saliva of the donkey are pure in themselves. However, when they mix with a small amount of water, the water becomes doubtful in its purifying capacity.
If no absolute water is available, one must perform both wudu and tayammum.
4
Apply the practical ruling
If a person only has doubtful sūr (e.g., water containing donkey saliva), he should: (1) perform wudu with it, preferably with intention, (2) then perform tayammum, and (3) pray. The prayer is certainly valid.
The order (wudu first) is preferred according to Zufar.
5
Refute invalid opinions
The passage rejects the baseless claim that the stallion's sūr is impure due to smelling urine, as it is not a predominant occurrence and does not affect the established purity.
This clarification protects against unnecessary strictness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و القسم الرابع سؤر مشكوك أي متوقف في حكم طهوريته (وحرمة لحمها النجس) الواو بمعنى مع قوله فلا كراهة فيه ولو ماتت في الماء قوله : (سؤر مشكوك) قال ابن أمير :حاج هذه التسمية لم ترو عن سلفنا أصلاً، وإنما وقعت لكثير من المتأخرين فسماه بعضهم مشكوكاً وبعضهم مشكلاً ومرادهم بذلك التوقف في كونه يزيل الحدث، فقالوا يجب استعماله التيمم عند عدم الماء المطلق احتياطاً ليخرج عن العهدة بيقين وليس معناه الجهل بحكم الشرع، كما فهمه أبو طاهر الدباس فأنكر هذا التعبير لأن الحكم فيه معلوم وهو ما ذكرنا والقول بالتوقف في مثل هذا لتعارض الأدلة دليل العلم وغاية الورع قال الحلبي : : وأما النجاسة الحقيقية فإنه يزيلها عند الإمام، وأبي يوسف لقلعه إياها حقيقة فصار كالخل بخلاف الحكمية قوله : (أي) متوقف في حكم طهوريته قال شيخ الإسلام خواهر زاده: الأصح أن دليل الأشكال هو التردد في الضرورة، والبلوى المسقطتين للنجاسة فإن الحمار يربط في الدور ويشرب من الأواني المستعملة، ويخالط الناس في ركوبه فأشبه الهرة في عدم إمكان مجانبته فسقطت نجاسة لعابه للحرج لكن ليست فيه كالضرورة في الهرة لأنها أشد مخالطة منه لدخولها في المضايق دون الحمار ، فلو لم يكن فيه ضرورة أصلاً، كان كالكلب في الحكم بالنجاسة بلا إشكال، ولو كانت الضرورة فيه كضرورة الهرة كان مثلها في سقوط النجاسة لذلك، وحيث ثبتت الضرورة من وجه دون وجه قيل بالشك في طهورية سؤره للاحتياط، وعدم الحرج في ذلك عملاً بالدليلين بقدر الإمكان وإعمال الدليلين أولى من إهمالهما عند عدم المرجح قال في البحر والمعتمد أن كلا من عرق الحمار، ولعابه ظاهر وإذا أصاب الثوب، أو البدن لا ينجسه، وإذا وقع في الماء القليل صار مشكوكاً وان الشك في جانب اللعاب والعرق أي في ذاتهما متعلق بالطهارة وفي جانب السؤر متعلق بالطهورية فقط، ولا شك في الطهارة لأن الماء ظاهر بيقين وقد خالطه مشكوك في طهارته، وهو اللعاب، أو العرق فلا ينجس، بالشك، ولكن أورث شكاً في طهوريته للاحتياط، حتى لو اختلط هذا السؤر بماء قليل جاز الوضوء به من غير شك ما لم يساوه، كما في مخالطة الماء المستعمل اهـ . قوله: (قلم يحكم الخ) أي فاحتجنا معه إلى التيمم لتحقق الرفع بمطهر يقيناً فلم يحكم بكونه مطهراً جزماً، ولم ينف عنه الطهورية وهو سؤر البغل الذي أمه أتان (والحمار) وهو يصدق على الذكر والأنثى لأن لعابه طاهر على الصحيح، والشك لتعارض الخبرين في إباحة لحمه وحرمته والبغل متولد من الحمار فأخذ حكمه (فإن لم يجد) المحدث (غيره) أي غير سؤر البغل والحمار (توضأ به وتيمم) والأفضل تقديم الوضوء لقول زفر بلزوم تقديمه والأحوط أن ينوي للإختلاف في لزوم النية في الوضوء بسؤر الحمار (ثم صلى) فتكون صلاته صحيحة بيقين لأن الوضوء به لو صح لم يضره التيمم وكذا قال من مشايخنا إن سؤر الفحل نجس لأنه يشم البول فتنجس شفتاه، فهو غير سديد لأنه أمر موهوم لا يغلب وجوده، ولا يؤثر في إزالة الثابت، ويستحب غسل الأعضاء بعد ذلك بالماء لإزالة أثر المشكوك والمكروه
And the fourth category: doubtful sūr, i.e., suspended in the ruling of its purifying capacity (and the impurity of its forbidden meat) – the waw means 'with' in his saying 'so no dislike in it' even if it dies in the water. His statement: (doubtful sūr). Ibn Amir said: This term was not originally transmitted from our predecessors, but occurred to many later scholars; some called it mashkūk (doubtful) and others mushkil (problematic). What they mean by that is being uncertain whether it removes ritual impurity. They say it is obligatory to use it for tayammum when there is no absolute water, as a precaution to exit from obligation with certainty. It does not mean ignorance of the legal ruling, as Abu Tahir al-Dabbas understood; he denied this expression because the ruling concerning it is known – it is what we have mentioned. And saying 'suspended' in such a case due to conflicting evidences is evidence of knowledge and utmost piety. Al-Halabi said: As for actual impurity (najāsah haqīqiyyah), it is removed by it according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf because it actually removes it, so it becomes like vinegar, unlike legal impurity (najāsah hukmiyyah). His statement: (i.e., suspended in the ruling of its purifying capacity). Shaykh al-Islam Kharzada said: The most correct is that the reason for the problem is the hesitation regarding necessity and widespread affliction that remove impurity. For the donkey is tied in houses and drinks from vessels used by people, and mixes with people through riding, so it resembles the cat in the impossibility of avoiding it. Thus, the impurity of its saliva is dropped due to hardship, but it does not have the same necessity as in the cat because the cat mixes more intensely, entering narrow places unlike the donkey. So if there were no necessity at all, it would be like the dog in being ruled impure without doubt. If the necessity were equal to that of the cat, it would be like it in dropping impurity. Since necessity is established from one aspect but not another, it is said there is doubt in the purifying capacity of its sūr, out of precaution and lack of hardship, acting on both proofs as much as possible. Acting on both proofs is better than neglecting them when there is no preponderance. Al-Bahr says: The relied-upon view is that both the sweat and saliva of the donkey are pure in themselves. If they touch a garment or body, they do not make it impure. If they fall into a small amount of water, it becomes doubtful. The doubt concerning saliva and sweat relates to their essential purity, while concerning the sūr it relates only to purifying capacity. There is no doubt about purity because the water is certainly pure in essence, and it is mixed with something whose purity is doubted (saliva or sweat). So it does not become impure due to doubt, but it creates doubt about its purifying capacity, as a precaution. Even if this sūr is mixed with a small amount of water, it is permissible to perform wudu with it without doubt as long as it does not equal it, as in the case of mixing with used water. End. His statement: (it is not judged...) i.e., so we need tayammum with it to achieve removal with a certain purifier. (It was not judged that it is absolutely a purifier, nor was purifying capacity denied from it) and it is the sūr of the mule whose mother is a domesticated donkey, and the donkey, which applies to male and female. Because its saliva is pure according to the correct view, and the doubt arises from the conflicting reports about the permissibility and prohibition of its meat. The mule is born from the donkey, so it takes its ruling. (If the person in need of ritual purification does not find) anything other than it, i.e., other than the sūr of the mule and donkey, (he performs wudu with it and tayammum) – and the best is to perform wudu first, based on Zufar's view of its necessity to be preceded. It is more precautionary to make intention because of the difference of opinion regarding the necessity of intention in wudu with donkey sūr. (Then he prays) – his prayer is certainly valid because if the wudu is valid, the tayammum does not harm it. Similarly, some of our mashāyikh said that the sūr of the stallion is impure because it smells urine and its lips become impure, but this is not sound because it is a baseless notion whose occurrence is not predominant, and it does not affect the removal of what is established. It is recommended to wash the limbs after that with water to remove the trace of the doubtful and the disliked.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This section deals with the fourth category of sūr: the doubtful sūr (sūr mashkūk). The Hashiya explains that this term was not used by early Hanafis; later scholars employed it to denote water whose ritual purifying capacity (ṭahūriyyah) is uncertain. The reason for doubt is the conflicting evidence regarding the donkey: its saliva is pure in itself, but there are contradictory hadith on the permissibility of donkey meat, and the necessity of avoiding hardship due to the donkey's constant contact with humans leads to a middle ground. The relied-upon position (al-muʿtamad), as stated in al-Bahr, is that the sweat and saliva of a donkey are pure; when they fall into a small amount of water, they do not make it impure, but they create doubt about the water's purifying capacity. Therefore, if a person only finds such water, he must perform both wudu (with that water) and tayammum, then pray. This ensures certainty of purification. The preferred order is wudu first, as per Zufar, and it is recommended to intend during wudu. After prayer, washing the limbs with pure water is recommended to remove any trace of doubt or dislike.

Key Terms
سؤر مشكوك (sūr mashkūk): Water whose purifying capacity (ṭahūriyyah) is uncertain due to conflicting evidences, even though its essential purity is not doubted.
طهورية (ṭahūriyyah): The quality of a substance to be inherently purifying (i.e., capable of removing ritual impurity).
تعارض الخبرين (taʿāruḍ al-khabarayn): Conflict between two reported hadiths, one permitting donkey meat and one prohibiting it, causing doubt in the legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person only has water that has been mixed with donkey saliva, what must he do to ensure valid purification?
A) Perform wudu with that water and pray.
B) Perform tayammum only.
C) Perform wudu with that water and then tayammum.
D) Combine the water with pure water to remove doubt.

Key Takeaway
When only doubtful sūr is available, combine wudu and tayammum to exit the obligation with certainty.
