The Doubtful Purity of Mule and Donkey Residual Water
Ruling on uncertain water purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the residual water of mules and donkeys, explain why its purifying status is doubtful, and apply the precautionary practice of combining wudu and tayammum when only such water is available.

Core Idea
When doubt surrounds water's purity, perform both wudu and tayammum to ensure valid prayer.

This passage addresses a practical problem: what if only water of uncertain purity is available? It explains that the residual water of mules and donkeys is a case of doubt due to conflicting hadith evidence. The Hanafi school prescribes a cautious procedure—combining wudu with this water and tayammum—to guarantee the prayer's validity regardless.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed item and its status
Find what the passage is discussing: the residual water (su'r) of mule and donkey. Note that it is 'not ruled as definitively purifying, nor is its purifying quality negated'.
The su'r is in a state of legal doubt (shakk).
2
Understand the cause of doubt
Recognise that the doubt arises from contradictory hadiths regarding the permissibility of eating donkey meat. Since the mule is born from a donkey, it takes the same ruling.
The saliva of these animals is considered pure (tahir) on the correct view, but the purifying capability (tahuriyya) of their residual water is uncertain.
3
Extract the obligatory precaution
When a person in a state of minor impurity (hadath) finds no other water except this su'r, they must perform both wudu with it and tayammum, then pray. This ensures the prayer is valid whether the wudu is accepted or not.
The combination is wajib (obligatory) in such circumstances.
4
Note the preferred order and intention
Zufr holds that wudu must precede tayammum. The text states the preferred order is wudu first. It also recommends making intention (niyyah) for wudu because of a difference of opinion on its necessity in this case.
Intention is recommended (mandub) but not obligatory for validity of wudu according to the preferred view.
5
Recognise the refuted opinion and after-wash
Some early Hanafi scholars claimed the su'r of a stallion is impure due to smelling urine, but the author rejects this as baseless—it is a hypothetical that does not predominate. It is recommended to wash the limbs with pure water after wudu to remove any trace of the doubtful.
The refutation shows the school's reliance on established rulings (thabit) over weak assumptions (mawhum).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلم يحكم بكونه مطهراً جزماً، ولم ينف عنه الطهورية وهو سؤر البغل) الذي أمه أتان (والحمار) وهو يصدق على الذكر والأنثى لأن لعابه طاهر على الصحيح، والشك لتعارض الخبرين في إباحة لحمه وحرمته والبغل متولد من الحمار فأخذ حكمه (فإن لم يجد) المحدث (غيره) أي غير سؤر البغل والحمار (توضأ به وتيمم) والأفضل تقديم الوضوء لقول زفر بلزوم تقديمه والأحوط أن ينوي للإختلاف في لزوم النية في الوضوء بسؤر الحمار (ثم صلى) فتكون صلاته صحيحة بيقين لأن الوضوء به لو صح لم يضره التيمم وكذا قال من مشايخنا إن سؤر الفحل نجس لأنه يشم البول فتنجس شفتاه، فهو غير سديد لأنه أمر موهوم لا يغلب وجوده، ولا يؤثر في إزالة الثابت، ويستحب غسل الأعضاء بعد ذلك بالماء لإزالة أثر المشكوك والمكروه
So it is not ruled as definitively purifying, nor is its purifying quality negated: it is the residual water of the mule whose mother is a she-donkey, and the donkey, which applies to male and female because its saliva is pure according to the correct view. The doubt is due to the contradiction of the two reports concerning the permissibility and prohibition of its meat. The mule is produced from the donkey, so it takes its ruling. If the person in a state of ritual impurity finds no other water except the residual water of the mule and donkey, he performs ablution with it and performs tayammum. The preferred order is to perform ablution first due to the statement of Zufr that it must be preceded. It is more precautionary to intend the ablution because of the difference of opinion regarding the necessity of intention in ablution with donkey residual water. Then he prays, so his prayer is certainly valid because if the ablution with it is valid, the tayammum does not harm him. Likewise, some of our scholars said that the residual water of the stallion is impure because it smells urine, so its lips become impure. But this is not sound because it is a hypothetical matter that does not predominantly occur, and it does not affect the removal of what is established. It is recommended to wash the limbs afterwards with water to remove the effect of the doubtful and disliked.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement regarding the residual water (su'r) of the mule and donkey. The author states that this water is not definitively purifying (tahur) nor is it definitively non-purifying; it is in a state of doubt. The reason for doubt is the conflicting hadiths about the permissibility of eating donkey meat—some indicate it is permissible, others that it is forbidden. Since the mule is born from a donkey, it follows the same ruling. The correct view is that the saliva of these animals is pure (tahir), but the purifying capability of their residual water is doubtful. When a person in a state of minor ritual impurity (hadath) finds no other water, he must perform both wudu with this water and tayammum, and then pray. His prayer will be valid with certainty because if the wudu is valid, the tayammum does not nullify it; if the wudu is invalid, the tayammum suffices. The preferred order is to perform wudu first, as stated by Zufr, and it is precautionary to make intention (niyyah) because of the differing views on whether intention is obligatory in wudu with donkey residual water. The text also refutes the opinion that the residual water of a stallion is impure due to smelling urine, calling it baseless. Finally, it is recommended to wash the limbs after wudu with pure water to remove any trace of the doubtful or disliked.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'r): The residual water left in a vessel after an animal or person has drunk from it.
طهور (tahur): A quality of water that is itself pure and capable of purifying other things.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the animal itself is impure.
B) Because of conflicting hadiths on the permissibility of its meat.
C) Because it is permissible to eat the meat.
D) Because the water is mixed with saliva.

Key Takeaway
The residual water of mules and donkeys is of doubtful purifying power, requiring a precautionary combination of wudu and tayammum when no other water is available.

Taharri for Mixed Water Vessels
Explains the rulings of taharri for mixed water vessels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when taharri is wajib for mixed water vessels and apply the correct ruling (wudu/ghusl vs. tayammum) based on the majority of pure vessels and the type of mixing.

Core Idea
Taharri is wajib only when pure vessels are in the majority; if equal, tayammum is obligatory.

When water vessels become mixed with impure ones, the Hanafi school requires taharri (estimation) to identify the pure water, but only under specific conditions. This lesson explains the rules for two types of mixing—commingling (mumazaja) and adjacency (mujawara)—and what to do when pure and impure vessels are equal in number.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of mixing
Determine whether the vessels are mixed by commingling (physical blending of waters) or by adjacency (vessels placed together). This affects the ruling.
Commingling requires estimation based on majority; adjacency treats all as impure if most are impure.
2
Assess the majority
Count the vessels. If the majority are pure, taharri is performed. If equal or majority are impure, different rules apply.
The text specifies 'most are pure' for taharri in wudu/ghusl.
3
Apply the ruling for commingling
If majority pure: perform taharri and use the estimated pure vessel for wudu/ghusl. If equal: do not estimate; instead perform tayammum because there is no definite purifier.
Some scholars (al-Tahawi) recommend mixing the waters; others (general mashayikh) recommend pouring them out, then tayammum.
4
Apply the ruling for adjacency
If the majority of adjacent vessels are impure, all are considered impure. Taharri is not performed except for drinking. One should pour out the water or mix it for animals, then perform tayammum.
The principle: the overcome (impure majority) is like non-existent.
5
Handle the case of two vessels without taharri
If one does not estimate but uses both waters for wudu and prays, the prayer is only valid if he wipes two different places on his head (each quarter). This accounts for the order of pure/impure usage.
This is a detailed scenario to show the importance of taharri.

فينتقل إلى التيمم لفقده المطهر قوله : (لا يتحرى إلا للشرب ولو اختلطت أوانيه، بأواني BestUrduBooks.wordpress.com
Chapter on Taharri (Estimation). If vessels are mixed, mixing of the opposite kind... and it is not disliked the residual water of an animal whose mother is edible, like a cow, wild donkey, and horse, nor eating it except the third according to the Imam's statement. His statement: 'Because his saliva is pure' is the cause for his statement 'doubtful in its purifying quality'. His statement: 'And the doubt' i.e., in its purifying quality. His statement: 'In the permissibility of its meat' – it is narrated that Abjar said: O Messenger of Allah, the year of drought befell us, and I have nothing in my wealth to feed my family except the fat of donkeys, and you have forbidden domestic donkeys. He said: Feed your family from your fat donkeys. His statement: 'And its prohibition' – Al-Bukhari narrated in the expedition of Khaybar from Anas that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was approached by a man who said: O Messenger of Allah, the donkeys have been eaten. He was silent. Then he came a second time and said: The donkeys have been eaten. He was silent. Then he came a third time and said: The donkeys have been finished. So he ordered a crier to announce among the people that Allah and His Messenger forbid you the meat of domestic donkeys. In another narration: 'for they are impure' so the pots were overturned while they were boiling with meat. The majority hold that the prohibition is for their very essence; it is said it was because they were jalalah (eating filth), or because they were the mounts of the people, or because they were finished before the division of the spoils. Shaykh al-Islam objected to this contradiction, saying it necessitates prohibition, not doubt, because then action is based on the prohibited. He corrected the direction of the contradiction by what we presented from him. His statement: 'If he finds no other water, even if the other is disliked, then it is certainly purifying.' His statement: 'He performs ablution with it and performs tayammum' is an addition with the letter waw indicating absolute conjunction to imply choice in precedence. His statement: 'The necessity of its precedence' because when ablution with it is obligatory, it resembles absolute water, and tayammum is valid in its presence, so likewise what resembles it, so ablution must be preceded to be devoid of water at the time of tayammum. His statement: 'And it is more precautionary to intend because its purification is weaker than absolute water, so it is strengthened by intention.' His statement: 'Then he prays' – he came with 'thumma' to indicate that prayer is after both acts, and this is preferred. If he prayed after each purification, the prayer is valid with dislike, and disbelief is not necessary because he did not pray without purification in every respect, but from one aspect without another; it is like a Hanafi praying after his iqtisad (following a lenient opinion), for he does not disbelieve, as purification remains according to the view of Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with them. His statement: 'And it does not affect the removal of what is established' i.e., with certainty, which is the purity of water. His statement: 'Chapter on Taharri' – it is exertion of effort to distinguish the pure from other. In the beginning of Sharh Muslim by al-Nawawi: tawakhkhi, ta'akhi, and taharra have the same meaning. Then, since mixing is of two types: mixing by commingling and mixing by adjacency. (Or if) the vessels (most of them are pure and the least impure, he estimates for ablution and bathing. It is restricted to the majority because he performs tayammum when the vessels are equal. The preferred is to mix them or pour them out, then perform tayammum due to definitely losing the purifying water. And if three men find three vessels, one of which is impure, and each estimates a vessel, their prayer individually is valid. Likewise, he estimates with majority pure for the purpose of drinking, because the overcome is like non-existent. If two vessels are mixed and he does not estimate, but performs ablution with each and prays, it is valid if he wipes two places on his head, not one place, because putting the pure first removes the hadath, and it becomes impure by the second, and one lacking purifier prays with impurity. And it becomes apparent by the second washing if he put the impure first and wiped another place on his head. Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement on the topic of taharri (estimation) when water vessels are mixed with impure ones. The chapter begins by defining taharri as exerting effort to distinguish pure from impure. Mixing is of two types: by commingling (mumazaja) and by adjacency (mujawara). If vessels are mixed by commingling and the majority are pure, one estimates for wudu and ghusl. If equal, one performs tayammum because the pure water is not predominant. The preferred action is to mix the waters or pour them out, then perform tayammum. If three men each find three vessels with one impure, each estimates and prays individually, and their prayer is valid. For drinking, one also estimates even if the majority is pure, because the overcome is like non-existent. If two vessels are mixed and one does not estimate, but uses both for wudu and prays, it is valid only if he wipes two different places on his head (each quarter) – the reasoning is given based on the order of pure and impure. If most vessels by adjacency are impure, one does not estimate except for drinking, and the water is poured out or mixed for animals, then tayammum is performed. For mixed garments (pure and impure), one estimates and does not repeat the prayer, because the garment has no substitute for covering the private parts.

Key Terms
تحري (taharri): Exerting effort and judgment to distinguish pure from impure when they are mixed.
اختلاط ممازجة (ikhtilat mumazaja): Mixing where waters are physically combined (commingling).
اختلاط مجاورة (ikhtilat mujawara): Mixing by adjacency, where vessels are placed together but contents not mixed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if he has two vessels of water, one pure and one impure, and he cannot determine which is which?
A) Perform wudu with both and pray.
B) Perform taharri and use the one he estimates to be pure.
C) Perform tayammum because the pure and impure are equal.
D) Mix the two waters and use the mixture.

Key Takeaway
Taharri is only wajib when pure vessels are in the majority; when they are equal, tayammum is obligatory.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
5 min
Taharri for Mixed Garments
States the ruling for taharri on mixed garments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for taharri when pure and impure garments are mixed and explain why no repetition is required.

Core Idea
For mixed pure and impure garments, taharri is performed, and the prayer is not repeated regardless of majority.

The previous lesson dealt with mixed water vessels; now we turn to mixed garments. The Hanafi ruling is simpler: one performs taharri to choose a garment, and does not repeat the prayer afterward, whether the majority were pure or impure. This lesson explains the rationale behind this leniency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The subject is mixed garments (thiyab mukhtalata) – some are pure, some are impure/najis.
Garments here refer to clothing needed for prayer covering the 'awrah.
2
State the ruling
One performs taharri to select a garment to wear for prayer. After praying, he does not repeat the prayer.
This applies regardless of whether the majority of garments are pure or impure.
3
Understand the reason
Unlike water, there is no substitute for covering the 'awrah. One must cover himself with something; taharri is the best effort. Even if the chosen garment turns out to be impure, the prayer is valid and not repeated.
The principle: no repetition (i'ada) is required because the garment has no alternative (la khalaf li al-thawb).

So he ordered a crier to announce among the people that Allah and His Messenger forbid you the meat of domestic donkeys. Taharri for Mixed Vessels by Adjacency
Passage states ruling for taharri when mixing by adjacency with majority pure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for taharri when vessels mixed by adjacency have a majority pure and apply the rule to scenarios of equal numbers.

Core Idea
When most vessels are pure, taharri is wajib; when equal, tayammum is required.

In Hanafi fiqh, when several vessels are in contact but not actually mixed (mujawara), and the majority are pure, one must perform taharri (estimation) to identify the pure water for wudu or ghusl. This lesson unpacks the conditions and exceptions from the classic text Maraqi al-Falah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine if the vessels are in adjacency (mujawara) or actual mixing (mumazaja). The ruling applies to adjacency where contents do not intermingle.
Mujawara means contact without mixing of contents.
2
Check the majority
Assess the number of pure vs impure vessels. If the majority is pure (e.g., 3 pure, 1 impure), taharri is wajib. If equal (e.g., 2 pure, 2 impure), taharri is not permitted; tayammum becomes wajib.
The condition 'most' (akthar) is critical.
3
Apply taharri for wudu/ghusl
Perform taharri by reasoning and signs to choose the likely pure vessel, then use it for wudu or ghusl.
Taharri is an act of ijtihad in purification.
4
Consider the preferred action
The text recommends mixing all water together or pouring it out, then performing tayammum to eliminate doubt.
This is a cautionary practice, not obligatory.
5
Apply the rule to other scenarios
The same taharri applies for drinking when pure vessels are abundant. Also, if three men each have one vessel with one impure, each performs taharri individually and their prayers are valid.
Each person's taharri is independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجاورة لا ممازجة (أو إن) جمع إناء (أكثرها طاهر) وأقلها نجس (تحرى للتوضؤ) والإغتسال قيد بالأكثر لأنه يتيمم عند تساوي الأواني والأفضل أن يمزجها أو يريقها فيتيمم لفقد المطهر قطعاً وإن وجد ثلاثة رجال ثلاث أوان أحدها نجس وتحرى كل إناء جازت صلاتهم وحدانا (و) كذا يتحرى مع كثرة الطاهر لإرادة (الشرب) لأن المغلوب كالمعدوم
By adjacency, not by mixing. Or if one gathers vessels, most of which are pure, and a few are impure, he performs taharri for wudu and ghusl. The condition of 'most' is given because when vessels are equal he performs tayammum. The best is to mix them or pour them out, then perform tayammum due to certain loss of purifier. And if three men have three vessels, one of which is impure, and each performs taharri, their prayers are valid individually. Likewise, he performs taharri when the pure is abundant for the purpose of drinking, because the outweighed is like non-existent.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn (Maraqi al-Falah) regarding vessels that are mixed by adjacency (mujawara) meaning they are separate but their contents come into contact, as opposed to actual mixing (mumazaja). When the majority of such vessels are pure water, one must perform taharri (estimation) to determine which vessel is pure for wudu and ghusl. The condition 'more' is specified because if the numbers are equal, one cannot perform taharri and must instead do tayammum. The preferred course of action is to mix all the water together or pour it out, then do tayammum, thereby ensuring no doubt remains. The passage also covers a scenario with three men and three vessels, one impure, where each performs taharri independently; their prayers are valid individually because each acts on his own estimation. Finally, for drinking purposes even when the pure vessels are many, taharri is performed because the small amount of impurity is considered non-existent (al-maghlub ka'l-ma'dum).

Key Terms
تحري (taharri): Estimation or attempt to determine the pure vessel through reasoning and signs.
مجاورة (mujawara): Adjacency or contact of vessels without actual mixing of their contents.
ممازجة (mumazaja): Actual mixing of the contents of vessels.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two vessels are mixed by adjacency (mujawara) and the majority are pure, what is the ruling regarding wudu?
A) One must perform tayammum.
B) One performs taharri and uses the estimated pure vessel.
C) One may use any vessel without taharri.
D) One must mix all water and then use it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when most vessels are pure and in adjacency, taharri is the required method to determine purity for wudu and ghusl, with tayammum reserved for equal numbers.

Vessels Without Taharri: Sequence and Conditions for Valid Wudu
Ruling on wudu with mixed vessels without taharri, focusing on head wiping conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which wudu with two mixed vessels (without taharri) is valid and identify the sequence required for valid prayer.

Core Idea
If wudu uses both vessels without taharri, prayer is valid only if two different head spots are wiped and pure water is used first.

This lesson examines a specific scenario where two water vessels are mixed and one cannot determine which is pure. Instead of performing taharri (investigation), the person uses both vessels for wudu. The Hanafi school lays out detailed conditions for the prayer to be valid, focusing on the sequence of use and the number of wipes on the head. Understanding these conditions clarifies the concept of 'one in need of purification praying with impurity.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person has two vessels, one pure and one impure, but does not know which is which. He does not perform taharri and instead performs wudu with both vessels.
This is a case of necessity due to uncertainty.
2
Check the number of head wipes
The key condition for prayer validity is whether the person wiped two different spots on the head (one with each water) or only one spot with the mixed water.
Wiping only one spot invalidates the prayer.
3
Analyze the sequence if two spots wiped
If two spots are wiped, the sequence matters: using pure water first removes hadath; using impure first requires a different spot for purification.
Pure first is always valid; impure first requires a different spot for the second wash.
4
Consider the one-spot case
If only one spot is wiped with both waters, validity depends on order but uncertainty leads to impermissibility.
Due to doubt, such wudu is not acceptable.
5
Conclude with precaution
To avoid doubt, the recommended action is to perform tayammum instead of using both vessels.
Tayammum is the precautionary alternative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن اختلط إنا آن ولم يتحر وتوضأ بكل وصلى صحت إن مسح في موضعين من رأسه لا في موضع لأن تقديم الطاهر مزيل للحدث، وقد تنجس بالثاني وفاقد المطهر يصلي مع النجاسة، وظهر بالغسل الثاني إن قدم النجس، ومسح محلاً آخر من رأسه، وإن مسح محلاً بالماءين دار الأمر بين الجواز لو قدم الطاهر، وعدم الجواز لتنجس البلل، بأوّل ملاقاة لو أخر الطاهر ، فلا يجوز للشك احتياطاً
And if two vessels are mixed and he did not perform taharri, and he performed wudu with each, and prayed, it is valid if he wiped two spots on his head, not one spot, because placing the pure first removes the hadath, and he becomes impure by the second, and one lacking a purifier prays with impurity. And purification appears by the second wash if he placed the impure first, and he wiped another spot on his head. And if he wiped one spot with both waters, the matter oscillates between permissibility if he placed the pure first, and impermissibility due to the impurity of the moisture upon first contact if he delayed the pure. So it is not permissible due to doubt, as a precaution.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling for a scenario where two vessels are mixed (by adjacency or actual mixing) and the person does not perform taharri but instead uses both vessels for wudu. If the person wipes only one spot on the head (which is the minimum for wudu), the prayer is not valid because the sequence matters. If he wipes two different spots, the prayer is valid provided he uses the pure water first and then the impure. The reasoning: if he starts with the pure, the hadath is removed. Then when he washes with the impure, his limbs become impure, but since he no longer has a purifier (the remaining water is impure), he prays with impurity, which is permissible in this state. If he starts with the impure, then the second wash with pure purifies, but he must wipe a different spot on the head to ensure removal of impurity. If he wipes the same spot with both waters, the validity depends on order. If he used pure first, it's permissible; if impure first, the moisture becomes impure on first contact and the purification is incomplete, so not permissible. Hence, precaution dictates not doing so and instead performing tayammum.

Key Terms
محل (mahall): A specific spot on the head (at least a quarter) for wiping.
بلل (balal): Moisture that transmits impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person uses both vessels without taharri and wipes one spot on the head, what is the ruling?
A) Prayer is valid regardless.
B) Prayer is valid only if pure first.
C) Prayer is not valid.
D) Prayer is valid with conditions.

Key Takeaway
In cases of uncertain water purity without taharri, valid wudu requires using both waters on separate head spots and observing the correct sequence.

Mixed Vessels with Majority Impure: Taharri Only for Drinking
Passage states that when majority is impure, taharri is only for drinking; internal dispute on disposal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when most vessels are impure, identify the only purpose for which taharri is allowed, and explain the two opinions on disposal of the impure water.

Core Idea
When impure vessels overwhelm, taharri is only for drinking; all water is impure, tayammum is required.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah addresses a classic scenario: you have several water vessels, some pure and some impure, but the impure ones are the majority. What do you do? The ruling distinguishes between the need for purification (wudu/ghusl) and the need for drinking water. Let's work through the legal reasoning and the internal Hanafi debate on how to dispose of the impure water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes vessels that are 'mixed by adjacency' (al-mukhtalata bi'l-mujawara), meaning they are separate vessels but placed near each other, some pure, some impure. The majority are impure.
This is not about mixing pure and impure water in one vessel, but about separate vessels.
2
Understand the legal effect of the majority
Because the impure vessels are the majority, all the water is legally considered impure (hukman li'l-ghalib). The principle is that the majority overrides the minority in determining the legal status.
This is a key usul principle: al-ghalib yu'ati hukmahu.
3
Identify the only allowed taharri
Taharri (estimation to find likely pure water) is only permitted for the purpose of drinking, not for wudu or ghusl. Since all water is considered impure, no vessel is likely pure enough for purification. Drinking is a necessity that allows relaxation.
For purification, tayammum is obligatory (as stated at the end).
4
Examine the two opinions on disposal
The water in the impure vessels must be disposed of. Two views: (1) The general mashayikh (majority of Hanafi scholars) say it should be poured out entirely. (2) Imam al-Tahawi says it can be mixed together and used to water animals.
The first opinion is considered more cautious (mufta bihi).
5
Conclude with the required act
After disposing of the water, one must perform tayammum for purification. Tayammum is wajib because no pure water is available.
The ruling is practical: no pure water for wudu/ghusl, so tayammum suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان أكثرها أي المختلطة بالمجاورة (تجساً لا يتحرى إلا للشرب) لنجاسة كلها حكماً للغالب فيريقها عند عامة المشايخ ويمزجها لسقي الدواب عند الطحاوي ثم يتيمم
And if most of them, i.e., those mixed by adjacency, are impure, he does not perform taharri except for drinking, because all are considered impure due to the majority. So he pours them out according to the general mashayikh, or mixes them for watering beasts according to al-Tahawi, then performs tayammum.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This ruling addresses the scenario where the majority of vessels (mixed by adjacency) are impure. In this case, all the water is legally considered impure due to the overwhelming impurity. Therefore, one should not perform taharri for purification (wudu/ghusl) because no vessel is likely pure. However, for drinking purposes, taharri is allowed because the need for water is greater. As for the impure water, the majority of scholars (general mashayikh) hold that it should be poured out entirely. Imam al-Tahawi holds that it can be mixed and used to water animals. After disposing of the water, one must perform tayammum for purification.

Key Terms
تحري للشرب (taharri li'l-shurb): Estimation to find potentially pure water for drinking, even when most vessels are impure.
حكماً للغالب (hukman li'l-ghalib): Legally, the majority determines the status of the whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When most vessels are impure, for which purpose is taharri allowed?
A) Wudu
B) Ghusl
C) Drinking
D) Tayammum

Key Takeaway
When impure vessels are the majority, all water is legally impure; taharri is only for drinking, and tayammum is obligatory for purification.

Mixed Clothes: Ruling on Taharri without Repetition
Hanafi ruling on mixed clothes: no repetition after taharri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mixed clothes and explain why no repetition (i'ada) is required.

Core Idea
After taharri for mixed clothes, prayer is valid and never repeated because clothing has no substitute.

When you have a mix of pure and impure garments and cannot tell them apart, the Hanafi school provides a clear rule: perform taharri (estimation) to choose, then pray. Your prayer is valid regardless of what you discover later. This lesson explains why there is no need to repeat the prayer, unlike cases involving water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the person has multiple clothes, some pure and some impure, and cannot determine the pure ones.
This applies whether the majority is pure or impure.
2
Required action: taharri
Before prayer, one must perform taharri (estimation) to select a garment most likely to be pure.
No other method like washing all clothes is required.
3
Ruling after prayer
The prayer is valid and does not require repetition (i'ada), even if the garment is later found to be impure.
This is absolute — no conditions on majority purity.
4
Understand the reason
The lack of substitute for clothing in covering 'awrah distinguishes it from water, which has tayammum as an alternative.
If a substitute existed, repetition might be necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وفي) وجود (الثياب المختلطة يتحرى) لا يعيد مطلقاً أي سواء كان أكثرها طاهراً أو نجساً لأنه لا خلف للثوب في ستر العورة،
And in the presence of mixed clothes, he performs taharri and does not repeat (prayer) absolutely, whether most of them are pure or impure, because there is no substitute for the garment in covering the 'awrah.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage discusses the case where one has multiple pieces of clothing, some pure and some impure, and cannot determine which is which. The ruling is that one must perform taharri (estimation) to select a garment to pray in, and once prayed, the prayer is valid and does not need to be repeated (i'ada). This applies regardless of whether the majority of clothes are pure or impure. The reason given is that, unlike water (which has a substitute in tayammum), there is no substitute for clothing in covering the 'awrah during prayer. Therefore, after taharri, the prayer is accepted and does not require repetition even if it later becomes clear that the garment was impure.

Key Terms
إعادة (i'ada): Repetition of prayer due to impurity discovered later.
تحرى (taharri): Estimation or effort to determine the pure garment when uncertain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when one has mixed clothes and prays after taharri, when is repetition (i'ada) required?
A) Only if the majority of clothes were impure.
B) Only if the majority of clothes were pure.
C) Never, absolutely.
D) Only if the exact garment is later found impure.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, once you perform taharri for mixed clothes, your prayer is valid and never requires repetition, because covering 'awrah has no alternative.

Change of Ijtihad after Prayer: Effect on Validity
Ruling on change of ijtihad after prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of prayers when ijtihad changes after a prayer has been performed.

Core Idea
Ijtihad once acted upon is final; a change of ijtihad does not retroactively affect past prayers.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a person has two garments mixed with impurity and uses ijtihad to determine which is pure, that ijtihad governs the prayer. But what happens if his ijtihad changes before the next prayer? This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies that the prior ijtihad remains in effect for the past prayer, and the new ijtihad cannot invalidate it. Only in the case of qibla does a change of ijtihad permit a fresh direction. Understanding this rule is essential for maintaining the continuity of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two garments, one likely impure. First prayer based on initial ijtihad. For second prayer, ijtihad changes.
2
Determine the ruling for the first prayer
First prayer is valid and not repeated.
3
Determine the ruling for the second prayer if he follows the new ijtihad
Second prayer is invalid if he prays in the garment now deemed pure according to new ijtihad.
4
Understand the legal reasoning (talil)
Implementation of ijtihad cannot be undone by its like (except for qibla). Impurity is a physical reality, not changed by ijtihad.
5
Note the exception for qibla
Qibla direction can change because it is a purely legal matter (shar'i).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن صلى في أحد ثوبين متحر بالنجاسة أحدهما، ثم أراد صلاة أخرى فوقع تحريه على غير الذي صلى فيه لم يصح لأنه إمضاء الاجتهاد لا ينقض بمثله إلا في القبلة لأنها تحتمل الإنتقال إلى جهة أخرى بالتحري لأنه أمر شرعي، والنجاسة أمر لا يصيرها طاهرة بالتحري للزوم الإعادة بظهور النجاسة بعد التحري في الثياب والأواني فمتى جعلنا الثوب طاهر بالإجتهاد للضرورة لا يجوز جعله نجساً باجتهاد مثله فتفسد كل صلاة يصليها بالذي تحرى نجاسته أولاً وتصح بالذي تحرى طهارته
And if he prayed in one of two clothes, having estimated one of them to be impure, then he intended another prayer and his estimation fell on the other than the one he prayed in, it is not valid because implementation of ijtihad is not undone by its like except in the qibla, because it admits of transfer to another direction by ijtihad since it (qibla) is a legal matter. And impurity is a matter that does not become pure by ijtihad, because repetition would be required upon the appearance of impurity after ijtihad in clothes and vessels. So whenever we declare a garment pure by ijtihad due to necessity, it is not permitted to declare it impure by a similar ijtihad. Thus every prayer he prays in the one he first estimated to be impure is spoiled, and the prayer in the one he estimated to be pure is valid.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a person has two pieces of clothing, and initially his ijtihad (estimation) indicates that one is impure and the other pure. He prays in the one he considers pure. Later, for a subsequent prayer, his ijtihad changes and he now considers the other to be pure and the first (which he used) to be impure. The ruling is that this new ijtihad does not override the first; the previous prayer remains valid, and the second prayer performed with the new ijtihad is not valid. The reason is that ijtihad once acted upon is established and cannot be undone by a similar ijtihad. This is different from the case of qibla direction, where one can change direction based on new ijtihad because qibla is a purely legal determination. Impurity, however, is a physical reality; ijtihad does not change the actual state. Therefore, the original estimation that the garment was pure is upheld for the past prayer, and the new estimation does not make the first garment impure retroactively. If he prays in the second garment based on the new ijtihad, that prayer is invalid because the first garment remains ritually pure for him in terms of his previous obligation.

Key Terms
إجتهاد (ijtihad): Personal reasoning or estimation to determine purity or qibla when evidence is unclear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person prays in a garment based on ijtihad, then later his ijtihad changes, what is the ruling on the first prayer?
A) It must be repeated.
B) It is invalid.
C) It is valid and not repeated.
D) It is valid but must be repeated if the new ijtihad is different.

Key Takeaway
Ijtihad once acted upon remains binding for past acts and cannot be overturned by a similar ijtihad, except for qibla.

The Three Types of Doubt (Shakk) in Taharah
Categorization of doubt with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of doubt and apply the Hanafi rule of original ruling (istishab) plus preponderance (ghalabah) to determine the ruling.

Core Idea
Doubt is resolved by the original ruling unless a majority indicates otherwise — the Hanafi way to certainty through preponderance.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi introduces a critical Hanafi principle for resolving uncertainty (shakk) in matters of purity and food. The author categorizes doubt into three types, each with its own rule. Understanding these types is essential for every Hanafi to navigate everyday situations where certainty is lacking.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the three categories of doubt
Doubt (shakk) is divided into three types: (1) doubt arising on an originally prohibited matter, (2) doubt arising on an originally permissible matter, and (3) doubt whose origin is unknown. Memorize these categories.
The third type requires ijtihad and is not detailed here due to page cutoff.
2
Apply the rule for Type 1 (originally prohibited)
If the original ruling is prohibition (e.g., meat from an unknown source), the doubt does not remove the prohibition unless a preponderant indication (such as a Muslim majority in the town) makes it permissible. Follow the example of the slaughtered sheep.
Preponderance (ghalabah) overrides the original prohibition.
3
Apply the rule for Type 2 (originally permissible)
If the original ruling is permissibility (e.g., water is pure by default), doubt (e.g., water has changed color) does not remove its purity unless impurity is confirmed. The water remains pure.
Istishab (continuation of original state) governs until evidence of change arises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه : مثل تعارض الخبرين الشك وقالوا إن الشك على ثلاثة أضرب شك طرأ على أصل حرام، وشك طرأ على أصل مباح وشك لا يعرف أصله، فالأول مثل أن يجد شاة مذبوحة في بلد فيها مسلمون ومجوس فلا تحل حتى يعلم أنها ذكاة مسلم لأن الأصل فيها الحرمة إذ حل الأكل يتوقف على تحقق الذكاة الشرعية، فصار حل الأكل مشكوكاً فلو كان الغالب فيها المسلمين جاز الأكل عملاً بالغالب المفيد للحل والثاني أن يجد ماء متغيراً،
Note: Similar to conflicting reports is doubt. They said doubt is of three types: doubt that arises upon an originally prohibited matter, doubt that arises upon an originally permissible matter, and doubt whose origin is unknown. The first is like finding a slaughtered sheep in a town where there are Muslims and Magians; it is not permissible until one knows that it was slaughtered by a Muslim, because the original ruling is prohibition, since the permissibility of eating is contingent upon verification of legal slaughter. So the permissibility of eating becomes doubtful. If Muslims are the majority in that town, then eating is permissible acting upon the majority which gives permissibility. The second is like finding water that has changed.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a note (tanbih) from the hashya, categorizing doubt (shakk) into three types applicable to taharah and food. The first type: doubt arises on an originally prohibited matter, such as finding a slaughtered animal in a mixed population. Since the default ruling for meat is prohibition, it remains haram unless there is clear evidence of lawful slaughter. However, if the majority of the population are Muslims, one may act upon the prevalent situation and consider it permissible. The second type: doubt on an originally permissible matter, such as finding water that has changed color, taste, or smell (indicating possible impurity). The original ruling for water is purity, so it remains pure unless impurity is confirmed. The third type (not described here due to the page cutoff) involves doubt where the original state is unknown. These principles help resolve cases of uncertainty based on the original ruling (istishab) and the preponderance of evidence.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Doubt about the purity or permissibility of an item.
أصل (asl): The original ruling or state of a matter (e.g., prohibition for meat, permissibility for water).
غالب (ghalab): Preponderance, majority – used as evidence to override the original ruling in cases of doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi categorisation of doubt (shakk), what is the ruling for Type 1 doubt (doubt on an originally prohibited matter) when the majority of the population are Muslims?
A) The item becomes permissible automatically.
B) The item remains prohibited because doubt cannot remove prohibition.
C) The item becomes permissible acting upon the preponderance (ghalabah) of Muslims.
D) The item requires further investigation; no rule applies.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, doubt is resolved by first identifying the original ruling and then, if possible, considering the preponderance of evidence.

Rulings on Impurity Falling into a Small Well
Lists cases requiring full emptying of a small well due to impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an impurity falls into a small well, and distinguish the cases of pig and dog based on their inherent impurity status.

Core Idea
A small well (<10x10 cubits) must be fully emptied if any impurity falls in; a dog triggers emptying only if it dies in the well.

This lesson from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the detailed rulings on impurities that fall into a small well. The text covers various types of impurities and animals, and clarifies the critical distinction between the pig (najis al-ayn) and the dog (not najis al-ayn in the relied-upon view). Understanding these cases ensures you can correctly determine when a well becomes impure and how to purify it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the well size
Determine whether the well is small (less than 10x10 cubits) or large. The ruling for small wells is strict: any impurity requires full emptying.
The definition of small well is a key condition; large wells have different rules.
2
Recognize the general rule
Any impurity falling into a small well, even a small amount like a drop of blood or wine, makes the entire water impure and requires complete emptying.
The quantity of impurity does not matter; even a trace triggers the obligation.
3
Distinguish inherently impure substances
Some substances are najis al-ayn (impure in essence), like the pig. Even if the pig exits alive without touching the water, the water becomes impure because of its inherent impurity.
Pig is considered najis al-ayn by consensus in the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the dog's special status
The dog is not najis al-ayn according to Imam Abu Hanifa (mufta bihi). Therefore, the well becomes impure only if the dog dies in it. If the dog exits alive without its mouth touching the water, the water remains pure.
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the Sahibayn consider the dog najis al-ayn like the pig.
5
Apply to other cases
The death of a sheep or a human in the well also requires full emptying. The text indicates that any animal death (except those explicitly excluded) necessitates nazh.
The exact scope of 'animal' is clarified in the commentary; the key principle is the presence of impurity.

في مسائل الآبار
كأصحاب فهو بهمزة بعد باء ساكنة، ومن العرب من يقدمها على الباء فتجتمع همزتان، فتقلب الثانية ألفاً ووزنه أفعال، وعلى الأول أفعال من بأر يبار باراً من باب قطع إذا حفر البؤرة بالضم الحفرة ومناسبة هذا الفصل لما قبله ظاهرة لأنه من جملة المياه. قوله: (والواقع فيها الخ ) يصح قراءته بالجر عطفاً على مسائل، وقوله: روث بدل منه، وبالرفع مبتدأ وروث الخ خبره، وعلى الأول فالعطف تفسيري لأن مسائل الآبار هي أحكام مائها إذا وقع فيها شيء مما ذكر قوله : ( ونحوه من كل نجس، ولو مخففاً لأن الغليظ والخفيف في المياه سواء قوله: (لأنه من إسناد الفعل إلى البئر) قصداً للمبالغة في إخراج الماء، وقوله : وإرادة الماء الحال بالبئر أشار به إلى أنه من إطلاق اسم المحل جميع وإرادة الحال فيه قوله : لأنه غير نجس العين على الصحيح هو قول الإمام رضي الله عنه، وعندهما نجس العين كالخنزير، والفتوى على قول الإمام، وإن رجح قولهما كما في الدر عن ابن الشحنة قوله : (أو) موت شاة هي اسم جنس يطلق على الضأن، والمعز كما في المصباح، والمراد أن تكون كبيرة في الجملة حتى لو كان ولد الشاة صغيراً جداً كان
On matters of wells. What falls into it: dung, an animal, or a drop of blood and the like. The ruling is that the well (i.e., its water) is emptied because the action is attributed to the well, meaning the water contained in the well (the small well), which is less than ten cubits by ten cubits, by the occurrence of impurity in it, even if the impurity is little, those that are not dung, and the little amount like a drop of blood or a drop of wine, because a little impurity renders a little water impure even if its effect is not visible. The well is emptied by the occurrence of a pig, even if it comes out alive and its mouth did not touch the water, due to the impurity of its essence. The well is emptied by the death of a dog, restricted to its death in it, because a dog is not najis al-ayn (impure in essence) according to the correct view. If it did not die, but came out alive, and its mouth did not touch the water, it does not become impure. Or the death of a sheep, or the death of a human in it, because of the emptying of Zamzam water... His statement (And what falls into it etc.) can be read in the genitive as an apposition to 'matters', or in the nominative as a subject, etc.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya Al-Tahtawi explains the rulings concerning impurities that fall into a well. It specifically addresses small wells (less than 10x10 cubits). The general rule is that if any impurity falls in, the entire well must be emptied, even if the impurity is small, like a drop of blood or wine. This is because a small amount of water is rendered impure by even a small impurity, even if no trace remains. The text then lists specific cases: a pig falling in requires emptying, even if it emerges alive without touching the water, because the pig itself is considered impure (najis al-ayn). A dog's death in the well also requires emptying, but if the dog does not die and exits alive without its mouth touching the water, the water remains pure. The commentary clarifies the difference between the view of Imam Abu Hanifa (that a dog is not najis al-ayn) and the view of his two disciples (that it is najis al-ayn like a pig). The fatwa is on the Imam's view, though some prefer the disciples' view. For sheep or human death in the well, the ruling is also emptying. The commentary also includes linguistic notes on the word 'bi'r' (well). This section is crucial for understanding the purity of water sources in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
بئر صغيرة (bi'r saghirah): A well whose dimensions are less than 10 x 10 cubits, which if impurity falls into it, the entire water must be emptied.
نزح (nazh): To completely empty the water from the well, usually performed when impurity falls into a small well.
نجس العين (najis al-ayn): A substance considered inherently impure by its very nature, such that contact with it causes impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a dog falls into a small well and exits alive without its mouth touching the water, what is the ruling?
A) The well must be fully emptied because a dog is najis al-ayn.
B) The water remains pure because the dog did not die and did not touch the water with its mouth.
C) The well must be emptied only if the dog is dead.
D) The water becomes impure regardless of whether the dog died or touched the water.

Key Takeaway
In a small well, any impurity requires full emptying; a dog is an exception—only if it dies in the well, because it is not inherently impure in the relied-upon view.

Taharah — Purification
advanced
12 min
Nazh of Small Wells: Impurities and Quantities
Critical refinement: Tahtawi explains and adjusts rulings on well purification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on draining a small well after impurity falls in, distinguish the required quantities for different types of impurities, and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the point of purification.

Core Idea
A small well must be fully drained after any impurity, but the required quantity varies by the type and state of what fell in.

This lesson covers the detailed Hanafi fiqh rules concerning wells (masa'il al-abiar). When an impurity falls into a small well (less than ten cubits in each dimension), the water becomes impure and must be drained (nazh). The amount of water to be removed depends on the type of impurity, whether it is an animal or liquid, and whether the animal was alive or dead, swollen or not. The lesson also addresses the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the precise moment the well becomes pure and on the estimate for abundant wells.

Guided Path
1
Identify well size and impurity type
Determine whether the well is small (less than 10 cubits in depth and width). Then identify the impurity: liquid (blood, wine) or animal (pig, dog, sheep, human, cat, chicken).
All impurities, even a single drop, require draining in a small well.
2
Determine the ruling of nazh
Nazh is wajib (obligatory) for all cases listed. For liquid impurities, the well must be drained completely if possible. For animals, the quantity depends on the animal's status and condition.
The obligation is based on the practice of the Companions and is established in zahir al-riwayah.
3
Apply specific quantities per case
For a pig (najis al-ayn): drain even if it exits alive without touching water. For a dog: drain only if it dies in the well (since it is not najis al-ayn). For a large sheep or human: drain fully. For a small animal (cat, chicken) without swelling: 40 buckets. For animals that swell or decompose: two hundred buckets (with recommended one hundred extra). For abundant wells where full drainage is impossible: two hundred buckets (Muhammad's estimate).
Two hundred buckets are medium-sized, commonly used in that well. If the animal is very small (like a lamb), treat as small animal? The text says even small requires draining due to spread of impurity, but some said 10 buckets, which is weak.
4
Identify the point of purification
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the well becomes pure when the last bucket separates from the mouth of the well. According to Imam Muhammad (in another view), it becomes pure when the bucket separates from the water. The fruit of the difference: water drawn before separation from the mouth is impure according to the Sahibayn but pure according to Muhammad.
The fatwa is on the more cautious view of the Sahibayn (separation from mouth).
5
Understand the estimation for abundant wells
Muhammad estimated two hundred buckets for abundant wells based on observation of Baghdad wells. Later scholars differ: some say the estimate should vary by locality, but the preferred view is to stick with two hundred for consistency and to prevent waswas. The more appropriate method, according to some, is to have two experts assess the water quantity.
The estimation is a rukhsah (concession) for wells that cannot be completely drained.

إلى غالب آبار البلد لكن في النهر أن التقدير بالمائتين مخرج على الغالب فليكن هو المعتبر لانضباطه تطميناً، وقطعاً للوسوسة كما اعتبروا في ذلك العشر، في العشر قوله : ( والأشبه) : أي بقواعد الفقه لكونهما نصاب
The Book of Purity: On issues of wells: and what falls into them of dung or an animal, or a drop of blood and the like, and its ruling is that the well is drained (i.e., its water) because it is an attribution of the action to the well, intending the water present in the well (the small well) which is less than ten by ten (by the occurrence of impurity) in it (even if the impurity is little, other than dung) and the small quantity (like a drop of blood or a drop of wine) because a small impurity contaminates a small amount of water even if its effect is not apparent. And (it is drained) by the occurrence of a pig even if it comes out alive while it did not touch the water with its mouth, due to the impurity of its substance. And (it is drained) by the death of a dog, restricted to its death in it because it is not impure in substance according to the correct view. So if it does not die, and comes out alive, and its mouth did not reach the water, it does not contaminate. Or (the death of) a sheep, or the death of a human in it, for the draining of Zamzam water like the treatment of one who... And it is possible that its change is due to impurity or long duration, it is permissible to purify with it based on the original purity. The third is the most that is forbidden, its sale is not forbidden where the prohibition of what he took from it is not confirmed, but it is disliked for fear of falling into the forbidden, as in Fath al-Qadeer, said by Abu al-Su'ud in Hashiyat al-Ashbah. It is: In issues of wells, like 'as'hab' so it is with a hamza after a silent ba, and some Arabs put it before the ba so two hamzas meet, so the second is turned into an alif and its measure is af'al, and according to the first it is af'al from ba'ara to dig a well. The suitability of this chapter to what came before is apparent because it is part of waters. His statement: 'and what falls in it' etc. can be read with jarr as an apposition to 'issues', and his word 'dung' is a substitute for it, or with raf' as a predicate and 'dung' etc. as the subject. According to the first, the apposition is explanatory because the issues of wells are the rulings of its water when something mentioned falls into it. His statement: 'and the like' of every impurity, even light because heavy and light are the same regarding water. His statement: 'because it is attribution of the action to the well' is for exaggeration in expelling water, and his statement: 'intending the water present in the well' indicates that it is a use of the name of the place to refer to what is in it. His statement: 'because it is not impure in substance according to the correct view' is the statement of the Imam, may Allah be pleased with him, and with them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is impure in substance like a pig, and the fatwa is on the Imam's statement, although they preferred their statement as in al-Durr from Ibn al-Shihnah. His statement: 'or death of a sheep' is a generic noun applied to sheep and goats, as in al-Misbah, and the intent is that it is large generally, so if the offspring of a sheep is very small, it would be (treated) like the death of a Zanjī, and Ibn Abbas and Ibn al-Zubayr, may Allah be pleased with them, commanded it in the presence of the Companions without denial. And (the well) is drained by the swelling of an animal even if it is small, due to the spread of impurity. And (it is) obligatory (to drain) two hundred medium buckets, which is commonly used in that well, and it is recommended to add one hundred. And if the obligatory amount is drained over days, or the impure garment is washed over days, it becomes pure. And the well becomes pure by the separation of the last bucket from its mouth according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Muhammad by its separation from the water, even if a drop fell into the well out of necessity, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said separation is required due to the remaining connection with the dripping drop. And Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, estimated the obligatory amount at two hundred buckets if it is not possible to drain it completely. And he gave a fatwa based on this because he observed that the wells of Baghdad had much water due to the proximity of the Tigris. And the more appropriate view is that its quantity be estimated by the testimony of two men knowledgeable about water, and this is the most correct. And if a chicken or a cat or the like dies in it (i.e., the well) without swelling, it is necessary to drain forty buckets after removing the dead body. The estimation by forty is narrated from... its ruling is the same as the cat. His statement: 'or death of a human in it' is based on the general state of the deceased not being free from impurity, otherwise it has passed that the washing of a clean deceased is only used water according to the correct view. So if he was clean, nothing is drained because of him, even before washing, that is narrated from Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar as in al-Qahastani from al-Muhit. So the author of al-Durr exempted the clean martyr only, but there is deficiency in it. And what he mentioned of detail regarding the Muslim: if he falls before washing, he contaminates; after it, he does not, is also based on the general state, mentioned by some virtuous scholars. I say: that is based on the view that the impurity of the deceased is khabath impurity, and it is also corrected, and the people of the madhhab have derived branches from each of them. His statement: 'and it is drained by swelling of an animal' meaning a blooded animal, not a watery one, and likewise if it disintegrates or its hair or feathers fall off. His statement: 'even if it is small' like a lamb (or kid), and some said: ten buckets are drained, but it is not strong. His statement: 'and it is what is commonly used in that well' is the apparent narration, and it is sufficient to fill most of the bucket and drain what is found even if little. His statement: 'and if the obligatory amount is drained over days' etc., and likewise if the obligatory amount is drained once. His statement: 'and they said separation is required' he repeated it to mention its evidence, and the fruit of the difference appears in the one who draws from it before separation from its mouth: it would be impure according to them, pure according to him (Muhammad). His statement: 'and Muhammad estimated the obligatory at two hundred buckets' is the easiest, and it is confirmed in al-Kanz, al-Multaqa, and al-Khulasa, and upon it is the fatwa, and it is the chosen as in al-Ikhtiyar, and it is preferred in al-Nahr and followed by al-Hamawi, and it is recommended to add one hundred for increased purity. His statement: 'if it is not possible to drain it' due to the abundant flow of water, so if it is possible to block the sources of water without hardship, it is necessary, then it is drained as done in Zamzam, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. His statement: 'and he gave a fatwa based on this because he observed that the wells of Baghdad had much water' meaning that despite their abundance, they did not exceed this amount. Al-Halabi said: Accordingly, one should not give a fatwa of two hundred absolutely, but rather look at the prevalent wells of the town. But in al-Nahr, the estimation by two hundred is based on the majority, so let it be the standard for its regularity and to cut off waswas (whispers), just as they considered the ten in ten. His statement: 'and the more appropriate' i.e., according to the rules of fiqh because both are nisab.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This is a commentary passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi expounding the rulings on wells from Maraqi al-Falah. The passage type is a critical refinement: Tahtawi clarifies and sometimes adjusts the base text. The core issue is the legal obligation (wujub) to drain water from a small well when impurity falls into it. A small well is defined as less than ten cubits in depth and width. The commentator explains that the obligation applies even to minute impurities such as a single drop of blood or wine, because a small amount of impurity renders a small amount of water najis even if no trace remains. Furthermore, the obligation is not limited to liquid impurities: the well must be drained if a pig falls in and comes out alive without its mouth touching the water, because the pig is intrinsically impure (najis al-ayn). As for a dog, the well is only drained if the dog dies in it, because the dog is not intrinsically impure on the correct view (that of Abu Hanifa). If it leaves alive without touching the water, it does not contaminate. The death of a large sheep or a human also necessitates draining. A key intra-Hanafi dispute appears regarding the purification of the well. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the well becomes pure when the last bucket separates from the mouth of the well. According to Muhammad (in another narration), it is purified when the bucket separates from the water itself. The fruit of this difference is that if someone draws water before the bucket separates from the mouth, the water is impure according to the Sahibayn but pure according to Muhammad. The required quantity of water to be drained is two hundred medium buckets (the size commonly used in that well), with a recommended additional one hundred. However, if the well is so abundant that it cannot be fully drained, the commentator notes that Muhammad estimated the obligatory amount at two hundred buckets based on his observation of Baghdad's wells. Some later scholars argue that the estimate should vary by locality, but the preferred view is to stick with two hundred for consistency and to prevent obsessiveness. For the death of a small animal like a chicken or cat without swelling, the required amount is forty buckets. The commentary also addresses the case of a human corpse: if the deceased is unclean, the well is drained; if he is pure (e.g., a martyr before washing), nothing is drained according to some narrations, though there is scholarly debate.

Key Terms
تنزح (tunzah): To drain or draw out water from a well (the well is drained) – a passive verb meaning the well's water is removed completely or to a specific quantity.
نجاسة (najasah): Impurity that prevents water from being pure and purifying, including both thick (ghaliz) and light (khafif) impurities.
بئر صغيرة (bi'r saghirah): A small well defined as less than ten cubits in depth and width.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if a dog falls into a small well and comes out alive without its mouth touching the water?
A) The well becomes impure and must be drained entirely.
B) The well becomes impure and forty buckets must be drained.
C) The well does not become impure because the dog is not impure in substance according to the correct view.
D) The well becomes impure and two hundred buckets must be drained.

Key Takeaway
A small well must be drained according to specified quantities after contamination, with intra-Hanafi differences on purification point and estimation for abundant wells.

The Obligation of Nuzuh and the Dispute on Purification: Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and the Point of Taharah
States obligatory nuzuh for swelling animal and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nuzuh for a swelling animal, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the moment of taharah, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Purification from a swelling animal's nijasah requires 200 buckets, but the precise moment of taharah divides the school: separation from mouth or from water.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a dead animal swells in a well, the water becomes impure and a prescribed number of buckets must be drawn. However, the exact moment when the well becomes pure after drawing is disputed between the two great students of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Their disagreement turns on whether dripping water re-establishes contact with impurity. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the relied‑upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is nuzuh (drawing water) from a well due to a swelling animal. The ruling is wajib: 200 medium buckets.
The obligation is for any swelling animal, even small, due to the spread of impurity.
2
State the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the well becomes pure when the last bucket separates from the well's mouth. Imam Muhammad alone holds that it suffices if the bucket separates from the water, even if water drips back.
Both views are transmitted within the school.
3
Analyze the evidence for each view
Both sides use rational proof (dalil aqli): the Sahibayn argue that dripping water maintains connection with impurity; Muhammad argues for concession due to necessity.
The text calls Muhammad's view a concession (darurah).
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
If a person uses water from the well before the bucket leaves the mouth, according to the Sahibayn it is impure; according to Muhammad it is pure.
This has practical implications for the validity of wudu or drinking.
5
Determine the tarjih and mufta bihi
Later Hanafi scholars adopt the view of the Sahibayn (separation from mouth) as more precautionary. The estimation by two expert witnesses is also recommended when draining is impossible.
The mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) تنزح بانتفاخ حيوان ولو كان صغيراً لانتشار النجاسة (و) تنزح وجوباً (مائتا دلو) وسط وهو المستعمل كثيراً في تلك البئر ويستحب زيادة مائة ولو نزح الواجب في أيام أو غسل الثوب النجس في أيام طهر وتطهر البئر بانفصال الدلو الأخير عن فمها عندهما، وعند محمد بانفصاله عن الماء ولو قطر في البئر للضرورة، وقالا يشترط الإنفصال لبقاء الإتصال بالقاطر بها، وقدر محمد رحمه الله الواجب بمائتي دلو (لو لم يمكن نزحها) وأفتى به لما شاهد آبار بغداد كثيرة المياه لمجاورة دجلة والأشبه أن يقدر ما فيها بشهادة رجلين لهما خبرة بأمر الماء، وهو الأصح
And one draws water due to the swelling of an animal, even if small, due to the spread of impurity. And one draws water as an obligation (200 medium buckets) – and it is that which is commonly used in that well. And it is recommended to increase by one hundred. And if he draws the obligatory amount over several days, or washes a najis garment over several days, it becomes pure. And the well becomes pure, according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), by the separation of the last bucket from its mouth; and according to Muhammad, by its separation from the water, even if water drips back into the well out of necessity. And they (the two) said that separation is required because connection remains with the dripping water. And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) estimated the obligatory amount as two hundred buckets (if it is not possible to drain it completely). And he gave fatwa according to that because he observed that the wells of Baghdad are abundant with water due to their proximity to the Tigris. And the more appropriate view is that its water be estimated by the testimony of two men who have expertise in water matters – and that is the most correct.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the ruling on a well when a swelling animal falls in. The matn states that drawing water is obligatory when an animal swells, due to the spread of impurity. The obligatory amount is 200 medium-sized buckets, with a recommended extra 100. The commentary then clarifies a key intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the well becomes pure only when the last drawn bucket separates completely from the well's mouth, because any dripping water re-establishes connection with the impurity. However, Imam Muhammad alone transmits that purification occurs when the bucket separates from the water itself, even if water drips back – this is a concession for necessity. Imam Muhammad also estimated the obligatory amount as 200 buckets, based on his observation of Baghdad's wells, and gave fatwa accordingly. The preferred view (al-ashbah) is that if the well cannot be drained due to abundant water, the amount should be estimated by two expert witnesses, and that is the most correct (al-asahh).

Key Terms
نزح (nazh): Drawing or bailing out water from a well to remove impurity.
منتفخ (muntafikh): Swollen – referring to an animal that has died and its body has swollen, indicating advanced putrefaction and spread of impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in the Hanafi school, when does a well become pure after drawing water for a swelling animal?
A) When the bucket separates from the well's mouth
B) When the bucket separates from the water
C) When the animal is removed
D) After 200 buckets, regardless of separation

Key Takeaway
The relied‑upon Hanafi view is that purification from a swelling animal requires drawing 200 buckets, and the well becomes pure only when the last bucket fully leaves the well's mouth.

Ruling for Chicken or Cat Dying in a Well
States the obligatory nuzuh for chicken/cat and provides hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory amount of water to draw when a small animal dies in a well and explain the evidence from hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
40 buckets are wajib for a chicken/cat-sized carcass; the proof is a hadith, and the obligation is wajib, not fard, due to zanni evidence.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah clarifies the Hanafi ruling for purifying a well when a small animal like a chicken or cat dies inside without swelling. You will learn the precise amount of water required and the distinction between the obligatory duty and the recommended increase.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the ruling
The case is a chicken or cat (or similar-sized animal) dying in a well without swelling. The ruling is that 40 buckets must be drawn after removing the carcass.
Note the condition 'without swelling' — a swollen carcass has a different ruling.
2
Identify the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that estimates 40 buckets for a chicken.
The hadith is ahad, giving zanni evidence.
3
Understand the qiyas extension
The ruling extends to animals similar in size to a chicken or cat, such as a cat, because the effective cause (illa) is the size and amount of impurity.
The Arabic term 'nahwihima' (similar to them) indicates the scope.
4
Distinguish wajib from mustahabb
The 40 buckets are wajib (obligatory) based on the ahad hadith; increasing to 50 or 60 is mustahabb (recommended) based on reports from 'Ata and al-Sha'bi.
Confusing the two levels is a common error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن مات فيها أي البئر دجاجة أو هرة أو نحوهما في الجثة ولم تنتفخ لزم نزح أربعين دلوا بعد إخراج الواقع منها، روي التقدير بالأربعين عن أبي سعيد الخدري في الدجاجة وما قاربها يعطي حكمها، وتستحب الزيادة إلى خمسين، أو ستين لما روي عن عطاء والشعبي
And if a chicken or a cat or similar dies in it (i.e., the well) in the carcass, and it did not swell, then it is necessary to draw forty buckets after removing the fallen animal. The estimation of forty is narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri concerning the chicken and what approximates it – it gives its ruling. And it is recommended to increase to fifty, or sixty, based on what is narrated from 'Ata and al-Sha'bi.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for a well when a chicken or cat (or similar-sized animal) dies without swelling. The obligatory amount is 40 buckets after extracting the animal. The proof is a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, which uses the chicken as an example, and the scholars extend the same ruling to animals of similar size. Two companions of the Prophet, 'Ata and al-Sha'bi, reported a recommendation to increase the amount to 50 or 60 buckets for extra precaution. The matn indicates the obligation is based on this evidence, while the increase is merely recommended (mustahabb).

Key Terms
الجثة (al-juththa): The carcass or body of the dead animal.
نحوهما (nahwihima): Similar to them (chicken and cat) – animals of approximately the same size and amount of impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Purifying a Well After a Mouse Dies
States the obligatory nuzuh for a mouse and the purification of bucket and rope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying a well after a mouse dies, explain the dalil, and apply the principle that purification of attached tools follows the water.

Core Idea
A mouse in a well requires 20 buckets; the well and its tools are purified as a unit.

When a small animal like a mouse dies in a well, the water becomes impure and must be removed. Imam al-Tahtawi explains the obligatory amount and the reasoning behind the purification of the well's equipment. This lesson unpacks the evidence from the hadith of Anas and the analogical reasoning that extends purification to the bucket and rope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and ruling
Note the conditions: a mouse or similar small animal dies without swelling. The ruling is that 20 buckets must be drawn.
The swelling condition is important; if the animal had swollen, a different amount applies.
2
Examine the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Anas: 'Twenty buckets are drawn.' This is an ahad hadith, so the ruling is wajib, not fard.
The recommendation to increase to 30 is based on a possible difference in bucket size in the original narration.
3
Understand the extension to tools
The purification of the well water automatically purifies the bucket, rope, pulley, and the drawer's hand because their impurity was derived from the water.
This is based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj) and analogy to wine vessel purification.
4
Apply the analogy
Just as a wine vessel becomes pure when the wine turns to vinegar, and a jug handle is purified when the hand is washed, the well tools are purified when the water becomes pure.
This shows that impurity is considered secondary to the source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن مات فيها فأرة بالهمز أو نحوها كعصفور، ولم ينتفخ لزم نزح عشرين دلوا بعد إخراجه لقول أنس رضي الله عنه في فأرة ماتت في البئر وأخرجت من ساعتها ينزح عشرون دلوا، ويستحب الزيادة إلى ثلاثين لاحتمال زيادة الدلو المذكور في الأثر على ما قدر به من الوسط وكان ذلك المنزوح طهارة للبئر، والدلو والرشاء والبكرة ويد المستقى روي ذلك عن أبي يوسف والحسن، لأن نجاسة هذه الأشياء كانت بنجاسة الماء فتكون طهارتها بطهارته نفياً للحرج، كطهارة دنّ الخمر بتخللها، وطهارة عروة الإبريق بطهارة اليد إذا أخذها كلما غسل يده
And if a mouse (with a hamzah) or something similar like a sparrow dies in it, and it did not swell, then it is necessary to draw twenty buckets after removing it, because of the statement of Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) concerning a mouse that died in a well and was taken out immediately: 'Twenty buckets are drawn.' And it is recommended to increase to thirty, due to the possibility that the bucket mentioned in the tradition (athar) may be larger than the medium bucket estimated here. And that drawn water is a purification for the well, and for the bucket, the rope, the pulley, and the hand of the drawer. That is narrated from Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan, because the impurity of these objects was due to the impurity of the water, so their purification follows its purification to remove hardship, just as the purification of a wine vessel through its turning into vinegar, and the purification of the handle of a jug through the purification of the hand when one takes it each time he washes his hand.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for a mouse or similarly small animal (like a sparrow) that dies without swelling. The obligatory amount is 20 buckets after removing the animal. The proof is a hadith of Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him), who reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered twenty buckets for a mouse taken out immediately. A recommendation to draw an extra ten (totaling 30) is mentioned due to a possible variation in bucket size in the original tradition. The commentary then explains that the drawn water purifies not only the well but also the bucket, rope, pulley, and the hand of the person drawing the water, because their impurity was secondary to the water's impurity. This is based on a narration from Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan, using the analogies of a wine vessel that becomes pure when the wine turns to vinegar, and the handle of a jug that is purified when the hand holding it is washed. This is to avoid hardship (raf' al-haraj).

Key Terms
الرشاء (al-risha'): The rope used to draw water from the well.
البكرة (al-bakarah): The pulley over which the rope runs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
